10 custody pursuant to NRS 432B.390. Such standards must consider the potential
11 harm to the child in remaining in his or her home, including, without limitation:
12 (a) Circumstances in which a threat of harm suggests that a child is in
13 imminent danger of serious harm.
14 (b) The conditions or behaviors of the child’s family which threaten the safety
15 of the child who is unable to protect himself or herself and who is dependent on
16 others for protection, including, without limitation, conditions or behaviors that are
17 beyond the control of the caregiver of the child and create an imminent threat of
18 serious harm to the child.
19  The Division of Child and Family Services shall ensure that the appropriate
20 persons or entities to whom the regulations adopted pursuant to this subsection
21 apply are provided with a copy of such regulations. As used in this subsection,
22 “serious harm” includes the threat or evidence of serious physical injury, sexual
23 abuse, significant pain or mental suffering, extreme fear or terror, extreme
24 impairment or disability, death, substantial impairment or risk of substantial
25 impairment to the child’s mental or physical health or development.
26 3. Regulations establishing procedures for:
27 (a) Expeditiously locating any missing child who has been placed in the
28 custody of an agency which provides child welfare services;
29 (b) Determining the primary factors that contributed to a child who has been
30 placed in the custody of an agency which provides child welfare services running
31 away or otherwise being absent from foster care, and to the extent possible and
32 appropriate, responding to those factors in current and subsequent placements; and
33 (c) Determining the experiences of a child who has been placed in the custody
34 of an agency which provides child welfare services during any period the child was
35 missing, including, without limitation, determining whether the child may be a
36 victim of sexual abuse or sexual exploitation.
37 4. Such other regulations as are necessary for:
38 (a) The administration of NRS 432B.010 to 432B.606, inclusive.
39 (b) The implementation of [NRS 125E.010 to 125E.370, inclusive,] chapter
40 127E of NRS and NRS 127.041, [127.115,] 127.151 , [and] 127.1861 [to 127.1869,
41 inclusive.] , 127.1863 and 127.1865, and sections 64, 74, 80, 86 to 90, inclusive,
42 127, 140, 144, 145 and 146 of this act.
43 Sec. 230. NRS 432B.393 is hereby amended to read as follows:
44 432B.393 1. Except as otherwise provided in this section, an agency which
45 provides child welfare services shall make reasonable efforts to preserve and
46 reunify the family of a child:
47 (a) Before the placement of the child in foster care, to prevent or eliminate the
48 need to remove the child from the home; and
49 (b) To make it possible for the safe return of the child to the home.
50 2. In determining the reasonable efforts required by subsection 1, the health
51 and safety of the child must be the paramount concern. The agency which provides
52 child welfare services may make reasonable efforts to place the child for adoption
53 or with a legal guardian concurrently with making the reasonable efforts required
Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 85
1 pursuant to subsection 1. If the court determines that continuation of the reasonable
2 efforts required by subsection 1 is inconsistent with the plan for the permanent
3 placement of the child, the agency which provides child welfare services shall make
4 reasonable efforts to place the child in a timely manner in accordance with that plan
5 and to complete whatever actions are necessary to finalize the permanent placement
6 of the child.
7 3. An agency which provides child welfare services is not required to make
8 the reasonable efforts required by subsection 1 if the court finds that:
9 (a) A parent or other person responsible for the child’s welfare has:
10 (1) Committed, aided or abetted in the commission of, or attempted,
11 conspired or solicited to commit murder or voluntary manslaughter;
12 (2) Caused the abuse or neglect of the child, or of another child of the
13 parent or other person responsible for the child’s welfare, which resulted in
14 substantial bodily harm to the abused or neglected child;
15 (3) Caused the abuse or neglect of the child, a sibling of the child or
16 another child in the household, and the abuse or neglect was so extreme or
17 repetitious as to indicate that any plan to return the child to the home would result
18 in an unacceptable risk to the health or welfare of the child; or
19 (4) Abandoned the child for 60 or more days, and the identity of the parent
20 of the child is unknown and cannot be ascertained through reasonable efforts;
21 (b) A parent of the child has, for the previous 6 months, had the ability to
22 contact or communicate with the child and made no more than token efforts to do
23 so;
24 (c) The parental rights of a parent to a sibling of the child have been terminated
25 by a court order upon any basis other than the execution of a voluntary
26 relinquishment of those rights by a natural parent, and the court order is not
27 currently being appealed;
28 (d) The child or a sibling of the child was previously removed from the home,
29 adjudicated to have been abused or neglected, returned to the home and
30 subsequently removed from the home as a result of additional abuse or neglect;
31 (e) The child is less than 1 year of age, the father of the child is not married to
32 the mother of the child and the father of the child:
33 (1) Has failed within 60 days after learning of the birth of the child, to visit
34 the child, to commence proceedings to establish his paternity of the child or to
35 provide financial support for the child; or
36 (2) Is entitled to seek custody of the child but fails to do so within 60 days
37 after learning that the child was placed in foster care;
38 (f) The child was delivered to a provider of emergency services pursuant to
39 NRS 432B.630;
40 (g) The child, a sibling of the child or another child in the household has been
41 sexually abused or has been subjected to neglect by pervasive instances of failure to
42 protect the child from sexual abuse; or
43 (h) A parent of the child is required to register as a sex offender pursuant to the
44 provisions of chapter 179D of NRS or the provisions of the federal Adam Walsh
45 Child Protection and Safety Act of 2006, 34 U.S.C. §§ 20901 et seq.
46 4. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 6, for the purposes of this
47 section, unless the context otherwise requires, “reasonable efforts” have been made
48 if an agency which provides child welfare services to children with legal custody of
49 a child has exercised diligence and care in arranging appropriate, accessible and
50 available services that are designed to improve the ability of a family to provide a
51 safe and stable home for each child in the family, with the health and safety of the
52 child as its paramount concerns. The exercise of such diligence and care includes,
53 without limitation, obtaining necessary and appropriate information concerning the
Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 86
1 child for the purposes of NRS 127.152, 127.410 and 424.038 , and section 81 of
2 this act, and, if necessary, creating an in-home safety plan for the protection of the
3 child.
4 5. In determining whether reasonable efforts have been made pursuant to
5 subsection 4, the court shall:
6 (a) Evaluate the evidence and make findings based on whether a reasonable
7 person would conclude that reasonable efforts were made;
8 (b) Consider any input from the child;
9 (c) Consider the efforts made and the evidence presented since the previous
10 finding of the court concerning reasonable efforts;
11 (d) Consider the diligence and care that the agency is legally authorized and
12 able to exercise, including, without limitation, the efforts to create an in-home
13 safety plan;
14 (e) Recognize and take into consideration the legal obligations of the agency to
15 comply with any applicable laws and regulations;
16 (f) Base its determination on the circumstances and facts concerning the
17 particular family or plan for the permanent placement of the child at issue;
18 (g) Consider whether any of the efforts made were contrary to the health and
19 safety of the child;
20 (h) Consider the efforts made, if any, to prevent the need to remove the child
21 from the home and to finalize the plan for the permanent placement of the child;
22 (i) Consider whether the provisions of subsection 6 are applicable; and
23 (j) Consider any other matters the court deems relevant.
24 6. An agency which provides child welfare services may satisfy the
25 requirement of making reasonable efforts pursuant to this section by taking no
26 action concerning a child or making no effort to provide services to a child if it is
27 reasonable, under the circumstances, to do so.
28 7. In determining whether reasonable efforts are not required pursuant to
29 subsection 3 or whether reasonable efforts have been made pursuant to subsection
30 4, the court shall ensure that each determination is:
31 (a) Made by the court on a case-by-case basis;
32 (b) Based upon specific evidence; and
33 (c) Expressly stated by the court in its order.
34 8. As used in this section, “in-home safety plan” means a plan created by an
35 agency which provides child welfare services to ensure the protection of a child in
36 [his or her] the home, including, without limitation, determining any vulnerabilities
37 of the child, managing any potential threats to the safety of the child and
38 determining the capacity of the person responsible for the welfare of the child to
39 care for the child.

51 Sec. 232. NRS 432B.580 is hereby amended to read as follows:
52 432B.580 1. Except as otherwise provided in this section and NRS
53 432B.513, if a child is placed pursuant to NRS 432B.550 other than with a parent,
Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 87
1 the placement must be reviewed by the court at least semiannually, and within 90
2 days after a request by a party to any of the prior proceedings. Unless the parent,
3 guardian or the custodian objects to the referral, the court may enter an order
4 directing that the placement be reviewed by a panel appointed pursuant to NRS
5 432B.585.
6 2. An agency acting as the custodian of the child shall, before any hearing for
7 review of the placement of a child, submit a report to the court, or to the panel if it
8 has been designated to review the matter, which includes:
9 (a) An evaluation of the progress of the child and the family of the child and
10 any recommendations for further supervision, treatment or rehabilitation.
11 (b) Information concerning the placement of the child in relation to the child’s
12 siblings, including, without limitation:
13 (1) Whether the child was placed together with the siblings;
14 (2) Any efforts made by the agency to have the child placed together with
15 the siblings;
16 (3) Any actions taken by the agency to ensure that the child has contact
17 with the siblings; and
18 (4) If the child is not placed together with the siblings:
19 (I) The reasons why the child is not placed together with the siblings;
20 and
21 (II) A plan for the child to visit the siblings, which must be presented
22 at the first hearing to occur after the siblings are separated and approved by the
23 court. The plan for visitation must be updated as necessary to reflect any change in
24 the placement of the child or a sibling, including, without limitation, any such
25 change that occurs after the termination of parental rights to the child or a sibling or
26 the adoption of a sibling.
27 (c) Information concerning the child’s education, including:
28 (1) A copy of any academic plan or individual graduation plan developed
29 for the child pursuant to NRS 388.155, 388.165, 388.205 or 388.227;
30 (2) The grade and school in which the child is enrolled;
31 (3) The name of each school the child attended before enrolling in the
32 school in which he or she is currently enrolled and the corresponding dates of
33 attendance;
34 (4) Whether the child has not completed or passed any course of
35 instruction that the child should have completed or passed by the time the report is
36 submitted, which has resulted in the child having a deficiency in credits;
37 (5) A copy of any individualized education program developed for the
38 child;
39 (6) A copy of any plan developed in accordance with section 504 of the
40 Rehabilitation Act of 1973, 29 U.S.C. § 794;
41 (7) A summary of any special education services received by the child;
42 (8) A copy of the most recent report card of the child;
43 (9) A statement of the number of credits earned by the child during the
44 most recent semester, if applicable;
45 (10) A statement of the number of times the child has been absent from
46 school during the current or most recent school year for which the child was
47 enrolled in school;
48 (11) The scores the child received on any academic assessments or
49 standardized examinations administered to the child;
50 (12) Any information provided by the educational decision maker
51 appointed for the child pursuant to NRS 432B.462; and
52 (13) Whether a request that the child receive special education services has
53 been made and, if so, the outcome of such a request.
Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 88
1 (d) A copy of any explanations regarding medication that has been prescribed
2 for the child that have been submitted by a foster home pursuant to NRS 424.0383.
3 3. Except as otherwise provided in this subsection, a copy of the report
4 submitted pursuant to subsection 2 must be given to the parents, the guardian ad
5 litem and the attorney, if any, representing the parent or the child. If the child was

15 If a person refuses to comply with or disobeys an order issued pursuant to this

17 5. The court or the panel shall hold a hearing to review the placement, unless
18 the parent, guardian or custodian files a motion with the court to dispense with the

20 from any report, statement or other information submitted to it.

22 432B.520, notice of the hearing must be filed with the court and must be given by
23 first-class mail or any other means agreed upon in writing between the agency
24 which provides child welfare services and the recipient of the notice to:
25 (a) All the parties to any of the prior proceedings;
26 (b) Any persons planning to adopt the child;
27 (c) A sibling of the child, if known, who has been granted a right to visitation
28 of the child pursuant to this section or [NRS 127.171] section 84 of this act and his
29 or her attorney, if any;
30 (d) Any other relatives of the child or providers of foster care who are currently
31 providing care to the child; and
32 (e) The educational decision maker appointed for the child pursuant to NRS
33 432B.462.
34 7. The notice of the hearing required to be filed and given pursuant to
35 subsection 6:
36 (a) Must include a statement indicating that if the child is placed for adoption
37 the right to visitation of the child is subject to the provisions of [NRS 127.171;]
38 section 84 of this act.
39 (b) Must not include any confidential information described in [NRS 127.140;]
40 section 37 of this act.
41 (c) Need not be given to a parent whose rights have been terminated pursuant
42 to chapter 128 of NRS or who has voluntarily relinquished the child for adoption
43 pursuant to NRS 127.040 [;] and sections 63 and 126 of this act; and
44 (d) Need not be given to a parent who delivered a child to a provider of
45 emergency services pursuant to NRS 432B.630.
46 8. The court or panel may require the presence of the child at the hearing and
47 shall provide to each person to whom notice was given pursuant to subsection 6 a
48 right to be heard at the hearing.
49 9. The court or panel shall, after considering the report provided in subsection
50 2 and any other relevant evidence, determine based on a preponderance of the
51 evidence:
52 (a) The continuing necessity for and appropriateness of the placement;
Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 89
1 (b) The extent of compliance with the plan submitted pursuant to subsection 2
2 of NRS 432B.540;
3 (c) Any progress which has been made in alleviating the problem which
4 resulted in the placement of the child;
5 (d) The date the child may be returned to, and safely maintained in, the home
6 or placed for adoption or under a legal guardianship; and
7 (e) Whether the child is making adequate academic progress and receiving the
8 educational services or supports necessary to ensure the academic success of the

A.B. No. 227—Revises provisions governing adoption. (BDR 11-928)
*A_AB227_R1_671*

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 3
ASSEMBLY BILL NO. 227–ASSEMBLYMEMBER MILLER
PREFILED FEBRUARY 3, 2025
_______________
Referred to Committee on Judiciary
SUMMARY—Revises provisions governing adoption. (BDR 11-928)
FISCAL NOTE: Effect on Local Government: May have Fiscal Impact.
Effect on the State: Yes.
~
EXPLANATION – Matter in bolded italics is new; matter between brackets [omitted material] is material to be omitted.
AN ACT relating to adoption; repealing, reenacting, revising, reorganizing and
establishing certain provisions relating to the adoption of children
through agency adoptions, identified adoptions, close-family
adoptions, confirmatory adoptions, readoptions and adoptions of
children placed in the custody of agencies which provide child welfare
services under certain circumstances; revising various provisions
relating to the adoption of adults; requiring the Division of Child and
Family Services of the Department of Health and Human Services to
adopt various regulations; directing the Legislative Counsel to make
various organizational changes concerning the placement of certain
compacts for adoption in the Nevada Revised Statutes; providing
penalties; and providing other matters properly relating thereto.
Legislative Counsel’s Digest:
1 Existing law establishes various procedures relating to the adoption of children. (Chapter
2 127 of NRS) Sections 48-153, [155-215] 156-215 and 239 of this bill remove, repeal, reenact,
3 revise, reorganize and establish provisions related to the adoption of children. Specifically,
4 sections [1-153] 2-153 and [155-215] 156-215 of this bill make various changes to provide:
5 (1) general provisions applicable to the adoption of children, regardless of the type of
6 adoption; (2) provisions governing the adoption of children in the custody of agencies which
7 provide child welfare services; (3) provisions governing confirmatory adoptions and
8 readoptions; (4) provisions governing close-family adoptions; and (5) provisions governing
9 agency adoptions, identified adoptions and adult adoptions.
10 Sections 2-46 encompass the general provisions applicable to all types of adoptions.
11 Sections 3-29 establish various definitions applicable to adoption proceedings. Section 239
12 repeals various provisions of general applicability, including certain provisions related to the
13 State Register of Adoptions, provisions governing adoption procedures, provisions concerning
14 the licensing of child-placing agencies and provisions related to certain prohibited conduct.
15 Sections 33-46 reenact similar or revised provisions for the purpose of placement in the
16 general applicability provisions.
17 Sections 171-173, 175-177, 183, 185-188, 190, 192, 194, 196-199, 208-212 and 239
18 generally remove and repeal various provisions related to the adoption of children in the
19 custody of agencies which provide child welfare services and close-family adoptions, thereby
20 retaining the procedures related to agency adoptions and identified adoptions in chapter 127 of
21 NRS.

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 4
22 Sections [2-46] 48-105 reenact similar, revised or new provisions for the purpose of
23 establishing provisions that independently govern adoptions facilitated by agencies which
24 provide child welfare services.
25 Additionally, sections 116-153 reenact similar, revised or new provisions for the purpose
26 of establishing independent procedures governing close-family adoptions.
27 Sections 108-111 establish procedures for confirmatory adoptions for the purpose of
28 authorizing a petitioner to confirm the parentage of a child under certain circumstances.
29 Sections 112 and 113 establish procedures for readoption which authorize certain
30 persons who adopt a child through intercountry adoption to petition the court to readopt the
31 child.
32 Existing law establishes the Interstate Compact on the Placement of Children and the
33 Interstate Compact on Adoption and Medical Assistance. (NRS 127.330, 127.410) Section
34 236 of this bill directs the Legislative Counsel, in the next reprint of the Nevada Revised
35 Statutes, to cause the transfer of each Compact to a new chapter of NRS, respectively.
36 Finally, existing law authorizes an adult to adopt another adult under certain
37 circumstances and establishes various procedural requirements related to such adoptions.
38 (NRS 127.005, 127.190-127.210) Sections [201-203] 193-205 of this bill make various
39 changes relating to the adoption of adults.
40 Sections 154 , 154.5 and 216-235 of this bill make conforming changes related to the
41 reorganization of the provisions governing adoption.
THE PEOPLE OF THE STATE OF NEVADA, REPRESENTED IN
SENATE AND ASSEMBLY, DO ENACT AS FOLLOWS:
1 Section 1. Title 11 of NRS is hereby amended by adding thereto a new
2 chapter to consist of the provisions set forth as sections 2 to 46, inclusive, of this
3 act.
4 Sec. 2. As used in this chapter, chapter 127 of NRS, the chapter consisting
5 of sections 48 to 105, inclusive, of this act, the chapter consisting of sections 107
6 to 114, inclusive, of this act and the chapter consisting of sections 116 to 153,
7 inclusive, of this act, unless the context otherwise requires, the words and terms
8 defined in section 3 to 29, inclusive, of this act have the meanings ascribed to
9 them in those sections.
10 Sec. 3. “Adoption” means a legally recognized procedure that creates a
11 parent-child relationship.
12 Sec. 4. “Adoption services” means services provided by an agency which
13 provides child welfare services or a child-placing agency, including, without
14 limitation:
15 1. Identifying a child for adoption and arranging an adoption;
16 2. Securing a specific consent to adoption, relinquishment or termination of
17 parental rights;
18 3. Performing a home study on a prospective adoptive parent and reporting
19 on the home study;
20 4. Making a determination of the best interest of the child and the
21 appropriateness of an adoptive placement for the child;
22 5. Conducting post-placement monitoring of a case until final adoption; or
23 6. Assuming custody and providing child care or any other social services
24 pending an alternative placement, if made necessary by a disruption before final
25 adoption.
26 Sec. 5. “Adult” means a person who is at least 18 years of age.
27 Sec. 6. “Adult adoption” means a type of adoption where the person being
28 adopted is an adult.

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 5
1 Sec. 7. “Agency adoption” means a type of adoption performed by an
2 agency which provides child welfare services or a child-placing agency, where the
3 agency which provides child welfare services or the child-placing agency:
4 1. Accepts temporary custody of a child until final adoption; and
5 2. Assists in and arranges the placement of a child for adoption by
6 matching birth parents with adoptive parents and providing adoption services.
7 Sec. 8. “Agency which provides child welfare services” has the meaning
8 ascribed to it in NRS 432B.030.
9 Sec. 9. “Arrange the placement of a child” means to make preparations for
10 or bring about any agreement or understanding concerning the adoption of a
11 child.
12 Sec. 10. “Best interest of the child” means the legal standard used to
13 ensure every decision made in the adoption process prioritizes stability, safety and
14 permanency of the child to be adopted.
15 Sec. 11. “Blind” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS 426.082.
16 Sec. 12. “Child” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS 128.0124.
17 Sec. 13. “Child-placing agency” means a nonprofit corporation organized
18 pursuant to chapter 82 of NRS and licensed by the Division to place children for
19 adoption.
20 Sec. 14. “Child with special needs” means a child for whom placement
21 with an adoptive parent is, in the opinion of the Administrator of the Division or
22 the designee of the Administrator, made more difficult because of the age, race or
23 number of siblings of the child, or because the child suffers from a severe or
24 chronic medical, physical, mental or emotional condition.
25 Sec. 15. “Close-family adoption” means a type of adoption where a
26 petitioner or the spouse of a petitioner is related to the child to be adopted within
27 the third degree of consanguinity.
28 Sec. 16. “Confirmatory adoption” means a type of adoption where the
29 petitioner is already a parent of a child either through a court order or
30 presumptively and is asking the court to confirm parentage through an adoption
31 or readoption.
32 Sec. 17. “Division” means the Division of Child and Family Services of the
33 Department of Health and Human Services.
34 Sec. 18. “Domestic partner” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS
35 122A.030.
36 Sec. 19. “Holder of a valid registry identification card” means a person
37 who holds a valid registry identification card as defined in NRS 678C.080 that
38 identifies the person as:
39 1. Exempt from state prosecution for engaging in the medical use of
40 cannabis; or
41 2. A designated primary caregiver as defined in NRS 678C.040.
42 Sec. 20. “Identified adoption” means an adoption where:
43 1. None of the prospective adoptive parents [is] are related within the third
44 degree of consanguinity to the child to be adopted; and
45 2. The prospective adoptive parents and at least one of the parents of the
46 child to be adopted are known to each other and such knowledge was not caused
47 by the actions of a child-placing agency.
48 Sec. 21. “Indian child” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS 125E.080.
49 Sec. 22. “Marital partner” means two persons, regardless of gender, who
50 are at least 18 years of age, not nearer of kin than second cousins or cousins of
51 the half blood, and not having a spouse living, who are joined in marriage.
52 Sec. 23. “Person” means a natural person.

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 6
1 Sec. 24. “Putative parent” means a person who is alleged or reputed to be a
2 parent of a child but whose parentage has not been legally established.
3 Sec. 25. “Readoption” means a type of adoption where the petitioner has
4 previously obtained an order of adoption on the child at issue from a court of
5 another country.
6 Sec. 26. [“Recommend the placement of a child” means to suggest to a
7 child-placing agency that a prospective adoptive parent be allowed to adopt a
8 specific child, whether born or in utero.] (Deleted by amendment.)
9 Sec. 27. “Sibling” means each of two or more children having one or both
10 parents in common.
11 Sec. 28. “Spouse” means a marital partner, domestic partner, civil partner,
12 registered partner, reciprocal beneficiary or other partner who has the same
13 rights, protections and benefits, and is subject to the same responsibilities,
14 obligations and duties under law, whether derived from statute, regulation, court
15 rule, administrative policy, common law or any other provision or source of
16 authority, as are granted to and imposed upon marital partners.
17 Sec. 29. “Third degree of consanguinity” means the familial relationship
18 between two persons who share a common ancestor within three generations,
19 including, without limitation, a parent, stepparent, sibling, grandparent, great-
20 grandparent, aunt or uncle.
21 Sec. 30. The requirements prescribed by sections [31] 32 to 46, inclusive, of
22 this act are applicable to:
23 1. Agency adoptions, identified adoptions and, as applicable, adult
24 adoptions governed by chapter 127 of NRS;
25 2. Adoptions of children who are placed with agencies which provide child
26 welfare services governed by the chapter consisting of sections 48 to 105,
27 inclusive, of this act;
28 3. Confirmatory adoptions and readoptions governed by the chapter
29 consisting of sections 107 to 114, inclusive, of this act; and
30 4. Close-family adoptions governed by the chapter consisting of sections
31 116 to 153, inclusive, of this act.
32 Sec. 31. [An adoptive placement occurs when:
33 1. A parent executes a specific consent for adoption or relinquishment; or
34 2. A child-placing agency grants physical custody of a child in its custody to
35 a prospective adoptive parent or parents for adoption.] (Deleted by amendment.)
36 Sec. 32. An order of adoption and decree of adoption are both final
37 judgments from judicial proceedings of a court granting a petition for adoption.
38 Sec. 33. 1. The Division shall maintain the State Register for Adoptions,
39 which is hereby established, in its central office to provide information to identify
40 adults who were adopted and persons related to them within the third degree of
41 consanguinity.
42 2. The State Register for Adoptions consists of:
43 (a) Names and other information, which the Administrator of the Division
44 deems to be necessary for the operation of the Register, relating to persons who
45 have relinquished a child for adoption or have consented to the adoption of a
46 child, or whose parental rights have been terminated by a court of competent
47 jurisdiction, and who have submitted the information voluntarily to the Division;
48 (b) Names and other necessary information of persons who are 18 years of
49 age or older, who were adopted and who have submitted the information
50 voluntarily to the Division; and
51 (c) Names and other necessary information of persons who are related
52 within the third degree of consanguinity to adopted persons, and who have
53 submitted the information voluntarily to the Division.

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 7
1  Any person whose name appears in the Register may withdraw it by requesting
2 in writing that it be withdrawn. The Division shall immediately withdraw a name
3 upon receiving a request to do so, and may not thereafter release any information
4 to identify that person, including the information that such a name was ever in
5 the Register.
6 3. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 4, the Division may release
7 information:
8 (a) About a person related within the third degree of consanguinity to an
9 adopted person; or
10 (b) About an adopted person to a person related within the third degree of
11 consanguinity,
12  if the names and information about both persons are contained in the Register
13 and written consent for the release of such information is given by the parent.
14 4. An adopted person may, by submitting a written request to the Division,
15 restrict the release of any information concerning the adopted person to one or
16 more categories of relatives within the third degree of consanguinity.
17 Sec. 34. Except as otherwise provided in NRS 125E.270, the district courts
18 of this State have original jurisdiction in adoption proceedings.
19 Sec. 35. The same petitioners may, in one petition, petition for the adoption
20 of two or more children, if the children are siblings.
21 Sec. 36. All petitions, reports and orders in adoption proceedings shall be
22 entitled only in the names of the adopting parties.
23 Sec. 37. 1. Except as otherwise provided in NRS 239.0115, all hearings
24 held in proceedings under this chapter, chapter 127 of NRS, the chapter
25 consisting of sections 48 to 105, inclusive, of this act, the chapter consisting of
26 sections 107 to 114, inclusive, of this act and the chapter consisting of sections
27 116 to 153, inclusive, of this act are confidential and must be held in closed court,
28 without admittance of any person other than the petitioners, their witnesses, the
29 director of an agency which provides child welfare services or a child-placing
30 agency, or their authorized representatives, attorneys and persons entitled to
31 notice by this chapter, chapter 127 of NRS, the chapter consisting of sections 48
32 to 105, inclusive, of this act, the chapter consisting of sections 107 to 114,
33 inclusive, of this act and the chapter consisting of sections 116 to 153, inclusive,
34 of this act, except by order of the court.
35 2. The files and records of the court in adoption proceedings are not open to
36 inspection by any person except:
37 (a) Upon an order of the court expressly so permitting pursuant to a petition
38 setting forth the reasons therefor;
39 (b) If a parent and the child are eligible to receive information from the State
40 Register for Adoptions pursuant to section 33 of this act; or
41 (c) As provided pursuant to subsections 3 to 6, inclusive.
42 3. An adoptive parent who intends to file a petition pursuant to NRS
43 127.1885 or 127.1895 or section 94, 96, 150 or 152 of this act, as applicable, to
44 enforce, modify or terminate an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact
45 may inspect only the portions of the files and records of the court concerning the
46 agreement for postadoptive contact.
47 4. A parent who intends to file a petition pursuant to NRS 127.1885 or
48 section 94 or 150 of this act, as applicable, to prove the existence of or to enforce
49 an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact or to file an action pursuant
50 to NRS 41.509 may inspect only the portions of the files or records of the court
51 concerning the agreement for postadoptive contact.
52 5. Upon the request of a sibling or adoptive child who wishes to enforce,
53 modify or terminate an order for visitation included in an order of adoption

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 8
1 pursuant to NRS 127.2827 or section 105 of this act, as applicable, the court shall
2 provide the case number of the adoption proceeding to the sibling and allow the
3 sibling to inspect only the portions of the files or records of the court concerning
4 the order for visitation.
5 6. The portions of the files and records which are made available for
6 inspection by an adoptive parent, parent or sibling pursuant to subsection 3, 4 or
7 5 must not include any confidential information, including, without limitation,
8 any information that identifies or would lead to the identification of a parent if
9 the identity of the parent is not included in the agreement for postadoptive
10 contact or order for visitation, as applicable.
11 Sec. 38. 1. Upon the entry of an order of adoption, the child shall become
12 the legal child of the persons adopting the child, and they shall become the
13 child’s legal parents with all the rights and duties between them of parents and
14 child.
15 2. By virtue of [such] an adoption , the child shall inherit from the adoptive
16 parents or their relatives the same as though the child were the biological child of
17 such parents and, in case of the death of the child intestate, the adoptive parents
18 and their relatives shall inherit the child’s estate as if they had been the child’s
19 biological parents and relatives . [in fact.]
20 3. After a parent has executed a specific consent to adoption or
21 relinquishment or the parental rights of the parent have been terminated, and the
22 court has entered an order of adoption [is entered, any] :
23 (a) The parent [who has signed a relinquishment or given specific consent to
24 terminate parental rights] is relieved of all parental responsibilities for the
25 adopted child and shall not exercise or have any rights over the adopted child or
26 the property of the adopted child [.] ; and
27 (b) The child does not owe [a] the parent [whose parental rights have been
28 terminated] any legal duty and may not inherit from [a] that parent [whose
29 parental rights have been terminated] or [the kindred] a relative of that parent.
30 4. Notwithstanding any other provisions to the contrary in this section, the
31 adoption of a child does not in any way change the status of the relationship
32 between the child and any parent who is a petitioner and whose parental rights
33 have not been terminated.
34 Sec. 39. Any person against whom any order or judgment is made or who is
35 affected thereby may appeal to the appellate court of competent jurisdiction
36 pursuant to the rules fixed by the Supreme Court pursuant to Section 4 of Article
37 6 of the Nevada Constitution from any order or judgment of the district court
38 made under the provisions of this chapter, chapter 127, the chapter consisting of
39 sections 48 to 105, inclusive, of this act, the chapter consisting of sections 107 to
40 114, inclusive, of this act and the chapter consisting of sections 116 to 153,
41 inclusive, of this act, in the same manner as in other civil proceedings.
42 Sec. 40. 1. Except as otherwise provided in this section, a person or entity
43 may not place, arrange the placement of, or assist in placing or in arranging the
44 placement of, any child for adoption without securing and having in full force a
45 license to operate a child-placing agency issued by the Division. This subsection
46 applies to agents, servants, physicians and attorneys of parents or guardians, as
47 well as to other persons [.] and entities.
48 2. This section does not prohibit a parent or guardian from placing,
49 arranging the placement of, or assisting in placing or in arranging the placement
50 of, any child for adoption if the placement is made pursuant to NRS 127.280,
51 127.2805 or 127.2815 or section 100 of this act.

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 9
1 3. This section does not prohibit an agency which provides child welfare
2 services from placing, arranging the placement of, or assisting in placing or in
3 arranging the placement of, any child for adoption.
4 4. This section does not prohibit a person [,] or entity, including a person
5 acting in the professional capacity of the person, from sharing information
6 regarding an adoption if money or other valuable consideration is not paid:
7 (a) For such information; or
8 (b) For any other service related to the adoption that is performed after
9 sharing the information.
10 Sec. 41. 1. The application for a license to operate a child-placing agency
11 must be in a form prescribed by the Division. The license must state to whom it is
12 issued and the fact that it is effective for 1 year from the date of its issuance.
13 2. The issuance by the Division of a license to operate a child-placing
14 agency must be based upon reasonable and satisfactory assurance to the Division
15 that the application for such license will conform to the standards established and
16 the regulations adopted by the Division pursuant to NRS 127.230 and section 98
17 of this act.
18 3. When the Division is satisfied that a licensee is conforming to such
19 standards and regulations, it shall renew the license, and the license so renewed
20 continues in force for 1 year from the date of renewal.
21 Sec. 42. 1. After notice and a hearing, the Division may:
22 (a) Refuse to issue a license if the Division finds that the applicant does not
23 meet the standards established and the rules prescribed by the Division for child-
24 placing agencies.
25 (b) Refuse to renew a license or may revoke a license if the Division finds
26 that the child-placing agency has refused or failed to meet any of the established
27 standards or has violated any of the rules prescribed by the Division for child-
28 placing agencies.
29 2. A notice of the time and place of the hearing must be mailed to the last
30 known address of the applicant or licensee at least 15 days before the date fixed
31 for the hearing.
32 3. When an order of the Division is appealed to the district court, the trial
33 may be de novo.
34 Sec. 43. 1. Any attorney licensed to practice in this State or in any other
35 state:
36 (a) May not receive compensation for:
37 (1) Taking part in finding children for adoption; or
38 (2) Finding parents to adopt children.
39 (b) May receive a reasonable compensation for legal services provided in
40 relation to adoption proceedings.
41 2. A child-placing agency shall report any violation of subsection 1 to the
42 State Bar of Nevada, if the alleged violator is licensed to practice in this State, or
43 to the bar association of the state in which the alleged violator is licensed to
44 practice.
45 3. Any person who violates the provisions of subsection 1 is guilty of a
46 misdemeanor.
47 Sec. 44. 1. Except as otherwise provided in [section] sections 43 and 99 of
48 this act, a person or entity who does not have in full force a license to operate a
49 child-placing agency may not request or accept, directly or indirectly, any
50 compensation or thing of value for placing, arranging the placement of, or
51 assisting in placing or arranging the placement of, any child for adoption.
52 2. A child-placing agency may accept fees for operational expenses.

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 10
1 Sec. 45. 1. Except as otherwise provided in NRS 200.463 to 200.465,
2 inclusive, and sections 43 and 99 of this act, a person or entity who, without
3 holding a valid license to operate a child-placing agency issued by the Division,
4 requests or receives, directly or indirectly, any compensation or thing of value for
5 placing, arranging the placement of, or assisting in placing or arranging the
6 placement of, any child for adoption is guilty of a category D felony and shall be
7 punished as provided in NRS 193.130.
8 2. The parents and the adopting parents are not accomplices for the
9 purpose of this section.
10 Sec. 46. 1. Except as otherwise provided in this section and sections 40
11 and 43 of this act, it is unlawful for any person or [organization] entity other than
12 an agency which provides child welfare services or a child-placing agency to [,
13 without holding a valid unrevoked license to place children for adoption issued by
14 the Division,] place, arrange the placement of, or assist in placing or in
15 arranging the placement of, any child for adoption.
16 2. Except as otherwise provided in this section, it is unlawful for any person
17 or [organization] entity to place an advertisement or offer to the public, by any
18 medium, that a child is available for adoption or that a child is sought for
19 adoption.
20 3. Subject to subsection 4, a child-placing agency may place an
21 advertisement in this State that:
22 (a) A child is offered or wanted for adoption; or
23 (b) The child-placing agency is able to place, locate or receive a child for
24 adoption.
25 4. A child-placing agency shall include in any advertisement concerning its
26 services a statement which:
27 (a) Confirms that the child-placing agency holds a valid, unrevoked license
28 issued by the Division;
29 (b) Indicates any license number issued to the child-placing agency by the
30 Division; and
31 (c) Indicates that only child-placing agencies licensed in this State may
32 legally provide adoption services under the laws of this State.
33 5. It is unlawful for any person or entity who purchases advertising space
34 or purchases broadcast time for the purpose of advertising adoption services to
35 fail to include in any publication or fail to include in the broadcast for such
36 advertisement the license number in this State of the child-placing agency or
37 agency which provides child welfare services placing the advertisement. This
38 section applies to paid and unpaid advertisements.
39 6. An agency which provides child welfare services and a child-placing
40 agency may publish on an Internet website or in any newspaper published in this
41 State or broadcast by television a photograph of and relevant personal
42 information concerning any child for whom an adoptive resource is needed.
43 7. A person or entity who violates the provisions of this section is guilty of a
44 category E felony and shall be punished [pursuant] as provided in to NRS
45 193.130.
46 8. A periodical, newspaper, radio station, Internet website or other public
47 medium is not subject to any criminal penalty or civil liability for disseminating
48 an advertisement that violates the provisions of this section.
49 9. As used in this section:
50 (a) “Advertise” or “advertisement” means a communication that originates
51 within this State by any public medium, including, without limitation, a
52 newspaper, periodical, article, notice, magazine, telephone book listing, outdoor
53 advertising, billboard, sign, radio, television or computerized communication

1 system, including, without limitation, electronic mail, an Internet website or an
2 Internet account, or any similar media.
3 (b) “Internet account” means an account created within a bounded system
4 established by an Internet-based service that requires a user to input or store
5 information in an electronic device in order to view, create, use or edit the
6 account information, profile, display, communications or stored data of the user.
7 Sec. 47. Title 11 of NRS is hereby amended by adding thereto a new chapter
8 to consist of the provisions set forth as sections 48 to 105, inclusive, of this act.
9 Sec. 48. As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise requires, the
10 words and terms defined in sections 49 to 55, inclusive, of this act, have the
11 meanings ascribed to them in those sections.
12 Sec. 49. “Foster home” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS 424.014.
13 Sec. 50. “Home study” means the investigation of a prospective adoptive
14 parent or parents to determine the suitability of the prospective adoptive home
15 pursuant to section 100 of this act.
16 Sec. 51. “Parent” means a person:
17 1. Who is a biological or legal parent of a child whose parental rights have
18 not been terminated by a court order or execution of a specific consent to
19 adoption or relinquishment;
20 2. Who is a putative parent or proven parent of a child;
21 3. Who is presumed to be the parent of a child;
22 4. Whose paternity or parentage has been established pursuant to chapter
23 126 of NRS; or
24 5. Whose parentage has been confirmed by a court order.
25 Sec. 52. [“Placing parent” means a parent who executed a specific consent
26 to adoption or relinquishment pursuant to this chapter.] (Deleted by
27 amendment.)
28 Sec. 53. “Prospective adoptive parent” means a person who has been
29 identified by an agency which provides child welfare services as an adoptive
30 resource but whose adoption petition has not been granted by the court.
31 Sec. 54. “Relinquishment” means a document executed by a person
32 pursuant to this chapter which:
33 1. Voluntarily terminates the parental rights of the person in the child to be
34 adopted; and
35 2. [Names] Places the child with an agency which provides child welfare
36 services [.] for adoption.
37 Sec. 55. “Specific consent to adoption” means a document executed
38 pursuant to this chapter by a parent whose rights have not been relinquished or
39 terminated, which authorizes the child to be adopted by a specifically named
40 person or persons, and provides for the retention of the parental rights until the
41 final adoption.
42 Sec. 56. In addition to the requirements prescribed in the chapter
43 consisting of sections 2 to 46, inclusive, of this act, the provisions of this chapter
44 govern the adoption of children who are in the custody of an agency which
45 provides child welfare services pursuant to chapter 432B of NRS.
46 Sec. 57. The Division shall establish a Register of Children with Special
47 Needs. The Register must include descriptive information on every child with
48 special needs for whom a prospective adoptive parent is not identified within 3
49 months after the child becomes available for adoption, but must not include any
50 personal information which reveals the identity of the child or the child’s parents.
51 A copy of the Register must be made available for review by prospective adoptive
52 parents at each office of the Division.

1 Sec. 58. 1. The Division shall prepare a booklet on adoption in this State
2 which includes the following information:
3 (a) The legal basis of adoption;
4 (b) The purpose of adoption;
5 (c) The process of adoption;
6 (d) The number of children who are waiting to be adopted, including
7 statistical information regarding:
8 (1) The gender and ethnic background of the children who are waiting to
9 be adopted;
10 (2) The number of children placed in foster homes who are waiting to be
11 adopted;
12 (3) The number of children with special needs who are waiting to be
13 adopted; and
14 (4) The number of siblings who are waiting to be adopted;
15 (e) The name and location of agencies in this State that place children with
16 adoptive parents;
17 (f) The number of prospective adoptive parents;
18 (g) A comparison of this State to the surrounding states regarding the
19 placement of children with adoptive parents;
20 (h) A comparison of the Division to other agencies in this State regarding the
21 placement of children with adoptive parents; and
22 (i) Any subsidies, assistance and other services that may be available to
23 adoptive parents and prospective adoptive parents, including, without limitation,
24 services for children with special needs.
25 2. The Division shall:
26 (a) Revise the information in the booklet annually; and
27 (b) Distribute the booklet to persons and organizations whose patients or
28 clients are likely to become involved with the process of adoption in this State.
29 The booklet must also be distributed to prospective adoptive parents and parents
30 considering relinquishing for or consenting to adoption.
31 3. The Division may accept gifts or grants to assist in the production and
32 distribution of the booklet.
33 Sec. 59. 1. Except as otherwise provided in chapter 125E of NRS and
34 sections 64, 74, 80 and 86 to [95,] 90, inclusive, of this act, a child of whom this
35 State:
36 (a) Is the home state on the date of the commencement of the proceeding; or
37 (b) Was the home state within 6 months before the commencement of the
38 proceeding,
39  may not be adopted except upon an order of a district court in this State.
40 2. As used in this section, “home state” means:
41 (a) The state in which a child lived for at least 6 consecutive months,
42 including any temporary absence from the state, such as a placement outside of
43 the state through the Interstate Compact on the Placement of Children pursuant
44 to NRS 127.320 to 127.350, inclusive, immediately before the commencement of a
45 proceeding; or
46 (b) In the case of a child less than 6 months of age, the state in which the
47 child lived from birth, including any temporary absence from the state.
48 Sec. 60. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 2:
49 (a) A child in the custody of an agency which provides child welfare services
50 may be adopted by one or more adults with whom the child is placed by the
51 agency which provides child welfare services and subject to the rules prescribed
52 by this chapter;

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 13
1 (b) A person adopting a child must be at least 10 years older than the person
2 adopted; and
3 (c) If the child is over the age of 14 years, the child must agree to the
4 adoption.
5 2. A court may approve the adoption of a child without regard to the age
6 difference of the child and a prospective adoptive parent if:
7 (a) The prospective adoptive parent is related to the child within the third
8 degree of consanguinity; and
9 (b) The court is satisfied that it is in the best interest of the child.
10 Sec. 61. Compliance with the requirements of the Interstate Compact on
11 the Placement of Children pursuant to NRS 127.320 to 127.350, inclusive, may be
12 performed by an agency which provides child welfare services [, a child-placing
13 agency] or an attorney licensed to practice law in this State.
14 Sec. 62. 1. One or more adults may petition the district court of any
15 county in this State for leave to adopt a child.
16 2. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 5, a married person not
17 lawfully separated from a spouse may not adopt a child without the agreement of
18 the spouse, if such spouse is capable of giving such agreement to the adoption.
19 3. If a spouse agrees to an adoption as described in subsection 2, such
20 agreement does not establish any parental rights or responsibilities on the part of
21 the spouse unless the spouse:
22 (a) Has, in a writing filed with the court, specifically agreed to:
23 (1) Adopting the child; and
24 (2) Establishing parental rights and responsibilities; and
25 (b) Is named as an adoptive parent in the order of adoption.
26 4. The court shall not name a spouse who agrees to an adoption as
27 described in subsection 2 as an adoptive parent in an order of adoption unless:
28 (a) The spouse has filed a writing with the court as described in paragraph
29 (a) of subsection 3; and
30 (b) The home of the spouse is suitable for the child as determined by a post-
31 placement investigation pursuant to section 75 of this act and a home study
32 investigation pursuant to 100 of this act.
33 5. The court may dispense with the requirement for the agreement of a
34 spouse who cannot be located after a diligent search or who is determined by the
35 court to lack the capacity to agree. A spouse for whom the requirement was
36 dispensed pursuant to this subsection must not be named as an adoptive parent in
37 an order of adoption.
38 6. The court may determine that a child has a legal relationship with more
39 than two persons who petition for the adoption of the child pursuant to this
40 section.
41 Sec. 63. Except as otherwise provided in section 72 of this act, a specific
42 consent to adoption proposed by a petition for adoption of a child is required
43 from:
44 1. Each parent of the child who is alive and whose parental rights have not
45 been terminated or relinquished; and
46 2. Any legal guardian of the person of the child appointed by a court of
47 competent jurisdiction.
48 Sec. 64. 1. If a petition for adoption of a child concerns the adoption of
49 an Indian child, unless the parental rights of the Indian child’s parents have
50 been terminated, consent in writing to the adoption must be given by the Indian
51 child’s parents. Such written consent must be filed with the court.
52 2. An Indian child’s parent may consent to the adoption of the Indian child
53 at any time not less than 10 days following the date of the Indian child’s birth by

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 14
1 executing the consent in person or by remote appearance before the court on the
2 record.
3 3. Before the execution of a parent’s consent under subsection 2, the court
4 must explain to the parent on the record in detail and in the language of the
5 parent:
6 (a) The right to legal counsel;
7 (b) The terms and consequences of the consent in detail; and
8 (c) That at any time before the entry of the order of adoption, the parent may
9 withdraw consent for any reason and petition the court to have the child
10 returned.
11 4. After the execution of a parent’s consent under subsection 2, the court
12 shall certify that the court made the explanation under subsection 3 and that the
13 parent fully understood the explanation.
14 5. At any time before the entry of an order of adoption, an Indian child’s
15 parent may withdraw the parent’s consent under this section. The withdrawal of
16 consent must be made by filing a written withdrawal with the court or by making
17 a statement of withdrawal on the record in the adoption proceeding. Upon entry
18 of the withdrawal of consent, the court must promptly notify the person or entity
19 that arranged the adoptive placement to regain custody and control of the Indian
20 child. A parent who withdraws consent may petition the court for the return of
21 the child.
22 6. As used in this section, “parent” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS
23 125E.130.
24 Sec. 65. An agency which provides child welfare services may accept a
25 specific consent for adoption or relinquishment.
26 Sec. 66. An agency which provides child welfare services to which a child
27 has been ordered or relinquished for adoption shall be responsible for the care of
28 the child in its custody, and shall be entitled to the custody and control of the
29 child at all times until a petition for adoption has been granted.
30 Sec. 67. 1. Each agency which provides child welfare services that,
31 pursuant to section 65 of this act, accepts a relinquishment shall make all
32 necessary inquiries to determine whether the child is an Indian child. If it is
33 determined that the child is an Indian child and that the child is a ward of a tribal
34 court, resides on a reservation or is domiciled on a reservation, the agency which
35 provides child welfare services shall so notify the child’s tribe in writing.
36 2. The Division shall adopt regulations establishing reasonable and
37 uniform standards for making the necessary inquiries to determine whether a
38 child is an Indian child.
39 3. For the purposes of this section, the domicile of an Indian child must be
40 determined in accordance with federal common law.
41 Sec. 68. 1. A specific consent to adoption or relinquishment executed in
42 this State, or executed outside this State for use in this State, is not valid unless it:
43 (a) Identifies the child to be adopted by name, if any, sex and date of birth;
44 (b) Is in writing; and
45 (c) Is acknowledged by the person signing the specific consent to adoption or
46 relinquishment before a judge or a clerk of the court having a seal, a notary
47 public or a justice of the peace.
48 (d) Contains, at the time of execution:
49 (1) For a specific consent to adoption, the name of the person or persons
50 to whom specific consent to adopt the child is given; or
51 (2) For a relinquishment, the name of the agency which provides child
52 welfare services.

1 Sec. 71. 1. A minor parent may execute a specific consent to adoption or
2 relinquishment [with] without a requirement for notification to or consent by the
3 parent or parents of the minor.
4 2. A specific consent to adoption or relinquishment executed by a minor
5 parent cannot be revoked or nullified based upon a minor parent becoming an
6 adult.
7 3. A specific consent to adoption or relinquishment cannot be revoked or
8 nullified by the executing parent unless the specific consent to adoption or
9 relinquishment was obtained under fraud, duress or undue influence and the
10 action to void the specific consent to adoption or relinquishment is brought
11 within 30 days of execution.
12 Sec. 72. The execution of a specific consent to adoption or relinquishment
13 by a parent shall not be necessary:
14 1. Where parental rights have been terminated by an order of a court of
15 competent jurisdiction;
16 2. Upon the death of the parent; or
17 3. Upon the termination of the parental rights of the parent through
18 operation of law by a birth father registry operated in another state.
19 Sec. 73. 1. A petition for adoption of a child may be filed at any time after
20 a child is legally free for adoption and upon the agreement of the agency which
21 provides child welfare services.
22 2. The petition for adoption must state, in substance, the following:
23 (a) The full name and age of the petitioners.
24 (b) The age of the child sought to be adopted and the date that the child was
25 placed with the petitioners.
26 (c) That it is the desire of the petitioners that the relationship of parent and
27 child be established between them and the child.
28 (d) If the petitioners desire to change the name of the child, the new name
29 desired.
30 (e) That the petitioners are fit and proper persons to have the care and
31 custody of the child.
32 (f) That the petitioners are financially able to provide for the child.
33 (g) That there has been a full compliance with the law in regard to
34 termination of parental rights, specific consent to adoption or relinquishment as
35 to all parents.
36 (h) That there has been a full compliance with sections 97 to 105, inclusive,
37 of this act.
38 (i) Whether the petitioners have reason to know that the child is an Indian
39 child.
40 (j) That there are no known signs that the child is currently experiencing
41 victimization from human trafficking, exploitation or abuse.
42 (k) Whether an agreement for postadoptive contact has been entered into by
43 the parent or parents of the child and the prospective adoptive parent or parents
44 of the child.
45 (l) Whether there is an order for visitation of a child by a sibling or other
46 relative.
47 3. An order of adoption may not be entered unless there has been full
48 compliance with sections 97 to 105, inclusive, of this act.
49 Sec. 74. 1. In addition to the requirements set forth in [NRS 127A.110,]
50 section 73 of this act, a petition for adoption of a child must contain:
51 (a) A declaration under penalty of perjury and documentation, as described
52 by the regulations adopted by the Division pursuant to section 89 of this act, of

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 18
1 the petitioners’ good faith efforts described in subsection 1 of NRS 125E.210 to
2 determine whether there is reason to know that the child is an Indian child;
3 (b) A statement as to whether the petitioner has reason to know that the child
4 is an Indian child; and
5 (c) If the petitioner has reason to know that the child is an Indian child:
6 (1) A declaration under penalty of perjury and documentation, as
7 described by the regulations adopted by the Division pursuant to section 89 of this
8 act, showing that the proposed adoptive placement complies with the
9 requirements under NRS 127E.350; or
10 (2) A statement that the petitioner is moving the court under subsection 3
11 of NRS 125E.350 for a finding, by clear and convincing evidence, that good
12 cause exists for alternative adoptive placement and a statement describing the
13 details supporting the assertion of the petitioner that good cause exists for the
14 alternative placement, as described in subsection 3 of NRS 125E.350.
15 2. A petition for adoption of a child must, if applicable, request the
16 following:
17 (a) A finding that the petitioner complied with the inquiry requirements
18 under subsection 1 of NRS 125E.210;
19 (b) A finding of whether there is reason to know that the child is an Indian
20 child; and
21 (c) If the court finds that the child is an Indian child:

31 within 30 days after filing the petition, the petitioner shall:
32 (a) Serve copies of the petition by registered or certified mail, return receipt
33 requested, together with the notice of proceeding in the form required under
34 subsection 3 of NRS 125E.220, to:
35 (1) Each tribe of which the Indian child may be a member or in which
36 the Indian child may be eligible for membership;
37 (2) The appropriate Regional Director of the United States Bureau of
38 Indian Affairs listed in 25 C.F.R. § 23.11(b), if the identity or location of the
39 child’s parents, Indian custodian or tribe cannot be ascertained; and
40 (3) The appropriate agency which provides child welfare services.
41 (b) File a declaration of compliance with the court, including a copy of each
42 notice sent, together with any return receipts or other proof of service.
43 Sec. 75. 1. A petition for adoption of a child must be filed with the clerk
44 of the court.
45 2. Unless waived by the court, the agency which provides child welfare
46 services shall make a post-placement investigation and report as provided in this
47 section.
48 3. [The] Except as otherwise provided in this section, an agency which
49 provides child welfare services shall, not less than [14] 7 days before the date of
50 the hearing for adoption finalization, submit to the court a written report
51 regarding the results of the condition of the child and suitability of the home of
52 the prospective adoptive parent or parents, which must contain, without
53 limitation, a specific recommendation for or against approval of the petition and

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 19
1 a statement of whether the child is a known Indian child, and shall furnish to the
2 court any other information regarding the child or proposed home which is
3 required by the court. The court, on good cause shown, may extend the time,
4 designating a time certain, within which to submit the report. The agency which
5 provides child welfare services may waive this report for a prospective adoptive
6 parent who is related to the child within the third degree of consanguinity.
7 4. If the court is dissatisfied with the report submitted by the agency which
8 provides child welfare services, the court may order an independent home study
9 to be conducted and a report submitted by an agency selected by the court. The
10 costs of the investigation and report may be assessed against the petitioner.
11 Sec. 76. Notice of the filing of a petition for adoption of a child must be
12 provided to all legal custodians or guardians of the child who are not a parent of
13 the child.
14 Sec. 77. The report of the agency which provides child welfare services
15 must not be made a matter of public record, but must be given in writing and in
16 confidence to the district judge before whom the matter is pending. If the
17 recommendation of the agency which provides child welfare services is adverse,
18 the district judge, before denying the petition, shall give the petitioner an
19 opportunity to rebut the findings and recommendation of the report of the agency
20 which provides child welfare services.
21 Sec. 78. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 2, the prospective
22 adoptive parent or parents, child to be adopted, representative of the agency
23 which provides child welfare services and counsel for the parties may attend by
24 telephone or [video] remote appearance, in lieu of attending in person, any
25 hearings held by the court concerning a petition for adoption.
26 2. The court may waive the attendance of a child to be adopted for good
27 cause shown.
28 Sec. 79. 1. If the court finds that the best interest of the child warrants
29 the granting of the petition, an order of adoption must be made and filed,
30 ordering that henceforth the child is the child of the petitioners. When
31 determining whether the best interest of the child warrants the granting of a
32 petition, the court shall give strong consideration to the emotional bond between
33 the child and the prospective adoptive parent. A copy of the order must be sent to
34 the Division by the petitioners within 7 days after the order is issued. In the order,
35 the court may change the name of the child, if desired.
36 2. Except as otherwise provided in this subsection, an order of adoption
37 may not be made until 6 months after the placement of child with the petitioners.
38 3. If the court is not satisfied that the proposed adoption is in the best
39 interest of the child, the court shall deny the petition and custody of the child
40 shall remain with the agency which provides child welfare services. The court
41 shall not deny a petition solely because the petitioner:
42 (a) Is deaf, is blind or has another physical disability; or
43 (b) Is the holder of a valid registry identification card.
44 4. After a petition for adoption has been granted, there is a presumption
45 that remaining in the home of the adopting parent is in the best interest of the
46 child.
47 Sec. 80. 1. An order entered pursuant to section 79 of this act must
48 include:
49 (a) A finding that the petitioner complied with the inquiry requirements
50 under subsection 1 of NRS 125E.210 to determine whether there is reason to
51 know that the child is an Indian child; and
52 (b) A finding that the child is or is not an Indian child.
53 2. In an adoption of an Indian child, the order must include:

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 20
1 (a) The birth name and date of birth of the Indian child, the Indian child’s
2 tribal affiliation and the name of the Indian child after adoption;
3 (b) If known, the names and addresses of the parents;
4 (c) The names and addresses of the adoptive parents;
5 (d) The name and contact information for any agency having files or
6 information relating to the adoption;
7 (e) Any information relating to tribal membership or eligibility for tribal
8 membership of the Indian child;
9 (f) The determination regarding the Indian child’s residence, domicile and
10 tribal wardship status as required under NRS 125E.250;
11 (g) A finding that the petitioner complied with the notice requirements under
12 subsection 2 of NRS 125E.220;
13 (h) If the adoptive placement and the parents entered into a postadoptive
14 contact agreement or the adoptive placement and the Indian child’s tribe has
15 entered into an agreement that requires the adoptive placement to maintain
16 connection between the child and the child’s tribe, the terms of the agreement;
17 and
18 (i) A finding that the adoptive placement complies with the placement
19 preferences under NRS 125E.350 or, if the placement does not comply with the
20 placement preferences under NRS 125E.350, a finding upon the petitioner’s
21 motion under subsection 3 of NRS 125E.350 that good cause exists for placement
22 contrary to the placement preferences.
23 3. For each finding or determination made under this section, the court
24 must provide a description of the facts upon which the finding or determination is
25 based.
26 4. Upon entry of the order of adoption of an Indian child, the court shall

28 pursuant to section 79 of this act, any affidavit signed by a consenting parent
29 requesting anonymity, and all other required information in accordance with 25

31 Sec. 81. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 3, the agency
32 which provides child welfare services shall provide the prospective adoptive
33 parents of a child with a report which includes:
34 (a) A copy of any medical records of the child which are in the possession of
35 the agency which provides child welfare services.
36 (b) Any information obtained by the agency which provides child welfare
37 services during interviews of the parent regarding:
38 (1) The medical and sociological history of the child and the parents of
39 the child; and
40 (2) Any behavioral, emotional or psychological problems that the child
41 may have. Information regarding any behavioral, emotional or psychological
42 problems that the child may have must be discussed in accordance with policies
43 established by an agency which provides child welfare services pursuant to
44 regulations adopted by the Division for the disclosure of such information.
45 (c) Written information regarding any subsidies, assistance and other
46 services that may be available to the child if it is determined pursuant to section
47 85 of this act that the child has any special needs.
48 2. The agency which provides child welfare services shall obtain from the
49 prospective adoptive parents written confirmation that the prospective adoptive
50 parents have received the report required pursuant to subsection 1.
51 3. The report required pursuant to subsection 1 must exclude any
52 information that would lead to the identification of the parent.

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 21
1 4. The Division shall adopt regulations specifying the procedure and format
2 for the provision of information pursuant to this section, which may include the
3 provision of a summary of certain information. If a summary is provided
4 pursuant to this section, the prospective adoptive parents of the child may also
5 obtain the information set forth in subsection 1.
6 Sec. 82. 1. After an order of adoption has been entered, the court shall
7 direct the petitioner or the attorney of the petitioner to prepare a report of
8 adoption on a form prescribed and furnished by the State Registrar of Vital
9 Statistics or the equivalent office in the state that issued the birth certificate. The
10 report must:
11 (a) Identify the original certificate of birth of the person adopted;
12 (b) Provide sufficient information to prepare a new certificate of birth for the
13 person adopted;
14 (c) Identify the order of adoption; and
15 (d) Be certified by the clerk of the court.
16 2. The agency which provides child welfare services shall provide the
17 petitioner or the attorney of the petitioner with any factual information which will
18 assist in the preparation of the report required in subsection 1.
19 3. If an order of adoption is amended or annulled, the petitioner or the
20 attorney of the petitioner shall prepare a report to the State Registrar of Vital
21 Statistics or the equivalent office in the state that issued the birth certificate,
22 which includes sufficient information to identify the original order of adoption
23 and the provisions of that order which were amended or annulled.
24 4. The petitioner or the attorney of the petitioner shall forward all reports
25 required by the provisions of this section to the State Registrar of Vital Statistics
26 or the equivalent office in the state in which the birth certificate was issued not
27 later than the 30 days after the date in which the order was entered, or more
28 frequently if requested by the State Registrar of Vital Statistics, together with any
29 related material the State Registrar of Vital Statistics may require.
30 Sec. 83. 1. A placing parent of a child may not bring an action to set
31 aside an adoption after a petition for adoption has been granted, unless a court of
32 competent jurisdiction has previously, in a separate action:
33 (a) Set aside the specific consent to adoption;
34 (b) Set aside the relinquishment of the child for adoption; or
35 (c) Reversed an order terminating the parental rights of the placing parent.
36 2. After a petition for adoption has been granted, there is a presumption for
37 the purposes of this chapter that remaining in the home of the adoptive parents is
38 in the best interest of the child.
39 3. As used in this section, “placing parent” means a parent who executed a
40 specific consent to adoption or relinquishment pursuant to this chapter.
41 Sec. 84. 1. Except as otherwise provided in sections 91 to 96, inclusive, of
42 this act, in a proceeding for adoption of a child, the court may grant a reasonable
43 right to visit to:
44 (a) A sibling of the child if the child is in the custody of the agency which
45 provides child welfare services and a similar right has been granted previously
46 pursuant to NRS 432B.580; and
47 (b) Certain relatives of the child only if a similar right had been granted
48 previously pursuant to NRS 125C.050.
49 2. The agency which provides child welfare services shall provide the court
50 which is conducting the adoption proceedings with a copy of any order for
51 visitation with a sibling of the child that was issued pursuant to NRS 432B.580.
52 3. The court may not grant a right to visit the child to any person other than
53 as specified in subsection 1.
