1 Sec. 85. 1. The agency which provides child welfare services may consent
2 to the adoption of a child under 18 years of age with special needs due to race,
3 age or physical or mental problems who is in the custody of the agency which
4 provides child welfare services by proposed adoptive parents when, in the
5 judgment of the agency which provides child welfare services, it would be in the
6 best interest of the child to be placed in that adoptive home.
7 2. The agency which provides child welfare services shall in a timely and
8 diligent manner:
9 (a) Schedule any evaluations necessary to identify any special needs the child
10 may have.
11 (b) If it determines that the child has any special needs:
12 (1) Notify the prospective adoptive parents:
13 (I) That they may be eligible for a grant of financial assistance
14 pursuant to this section; and
15 (II) The manner in which to apply for such financial assistance; and
16 (2) Assist the prospective adoptive parents in applying for and satisfying
17 any other prerequisites necessary to obtain a grant of financial assistance
18 pursuant to this section and any other relevant subsidies and services which may
19 be available.
20 3. The agency which provides child welfare services may grant financial
21 assistance for attorney’s fees in the adoption proceeding, for maintenance and
22 for preexisting physical or mental conditions to the adoptive parents of a child
23 with special needs out of money provided for that purpose if the head of the
24 agency which provides child welfare services or the designee has reviewed and
25 approved in writing the grant of financial assistance.
26 4. The grant of financial assistance must be limited, both as to amount and
27 duration, by agreement in writing between the agency which provides child
28 welfare services and the prospective adoptive parents. Such an agreement must
29 not become effective before the entry of the order of adoption.
30 5. Any grant of financial assistance must be reviewed and evaluated at least
31 once annually by the agency which provides child welfare services. The
32 evaluation must be presented for approval to the head of the agency which
33 provides child welfare services or the designee. Financial assistance must be
34 discontinued immediately upon written notification to the adoptive parents by the
35 agency which provides child welfare services that continued assistance is denied.
36 6. All financial assistance provided under this section ceases immediately
37 when the child:
38 (a) Reaches 18 years of age, if the child is not enrolled in school, or 19 years
39 of age, if the child is enrolled in school;
40 (b) Graduates from high school, if the child is at least 18 years of age;
41 (c) Becomes self-supporting;
42 (d) Is emancipated; or
43 (e) Dies.
44 7. Neither a grant of financial assistance pursuant to this section nor any
45 discontinuance of such assistance affects the legal status or respective obligations
46 of any party to the adoption.
47 8. A court shall waive all court costs of the prospective adoptive parents in
48 an adoption proceeding for a child with special needs if the agency which
49 provides child welfare services consents to the adoption of such a child pursuant
50 to this section.
51 9. The Division, in consultation with each agency which provides child
52 welfare services, shall adopt regulations regarding eligibility for and the

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 23
1 procedures for applying for a grant of financial assistance pursuant to this
2 section.
3 Sec. 86. 1. A petition to vacate an order of adoption of an Indian child
4 under this chapter may be filed in a court of competent jurisdiction by a parent
5 who consented to the adoption.
6 2. Upon the filing of a petition under this section, the court shall set a time
7 for a hearing on the petition and provide notice of the petition and hearing to
8 each party to the adoption proceeding and to the Indian child’s tribe.
9 3. After a hearing on the petition, the court shall vacate the order of
10 adoption if:
11 (a) The petition is filed not later than 2 years following the date of the order;
12 and
13 (b) The court finds by clear and convincing evidence that the parent’s
14 consent was obtained through fraud or duress.
15 4. When the court vacates an order of adoption under this section, the court
16 shall also order that the parental rights of the parent whose consent the court
17 found was obtained through fraud or duress be restored. The order restoring
18 parental rights under this section must include a plan for the physical custody of
19 the Indian child, whether the Indian child will be placed with an agency which
20 provides child welfare services or with the parent.
21 Sec. 87. 1. If an order of adoption of an Indian child under this chapter
22 is vacated, the court vacating the order must notify, by registered or certified mail
23 with return receipt requested, the Indian child’s former parents, prior Indian
24 custodian, if any, and Indian tribe and the appropriate agency which provides
25 child welfare services.
26 2. The notice required under subsection 1 must:
27 (a) Include the Indian child’s current name and any former names as
28 reflected in the court record;
29 (b) Inform the recipient of the right to move the court for the return of
30 custody of and restoration of parental rights to the Indian child, if appropriate,
31 under this section;
32 (c) Provide sufficient information to allow the recipient to participate in any
33 scheduled hearings; and
34 (d) Be sent to the last known address in the court record.
35 3. An Indian child’s former parent or prior Indian custodian may waive
36 notice under this section by executing a waiver of notice in person before the
37 court and filing the waiver with the court. The waiver must clearly set out any
38 conditions to the waiver. Before the execution of the waiver, the court must
39 explain to the former parent or prior Indian custodian, on the record in detail
40 and in the language of the former parent or prior Indian custodian:
41 (a) The former parent’s right to legal counsel, if applicable;
42 (b) The terms and consequences of the waiver; and
43 (c) How the waiver may be revoked.
44 4. After execution of the waiver pursuant to subsection 3, the court shall
45 certify that it provided the explanation as required under subsection 3 and that
46 the former parent or prior Indian custodian fully understood the explanation.
47 5. At any time before the entry of an order of adoption of an Indian child,
48 the former parent or prior Indian custodian may revoke a waiver executed by the
49 former parent or prior Indian custodian pursuant to subsection 3 by filing a
50 written revocation with the court or by making a statement of revocation on the
51 record in a proceeding for the adoption of the Indian child.
52 6. If an order of adoption of an Indian child under this chapter is vacated
53 other than as provided in NRS 125E.360, an Indian child’s former parent or

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 24
1 prior Indian custodian may intervene in the proceeding and move the court for
2 the Indian child to be returned to the custody of the former parent or prior Indian
3 custodian and for the parental rights to the Indian child to be restored. The
4 moving party shall provide by registered or certified mail, return receipt
5 requested, notice of the motion for the Indian child to be returned to the custody

18 Sec. 90. 1. If the court determines that tribal customary adoption is in the
19 best interest, as described in NRS 125E.230, of a ward who is an Indian child and
20 the Indian child’s tribe consents to the tribal customary adoption:
21 (a) The appropriate agency which provides child welfare services shall
22 provide the Indian child’s tribe and the proposed tribal customary adoptive
23 parents with a written report on the Indian child, including, without limitation, to
24 the extent not otherwise prohibited by state or federal law, the medical
25 background, if known, of the Indian child’s parents, and the Indian child’s
26 educational information, developmental history and medical background,
27 including all known diagnostic information, current medical reports and any
28 psychological evaluations.
29 (b) The court shall accept a tribal customary adoptive home study conducted
30 by the Indian child’s tribe if the home study:
31 (1) Includes federal criminal background checks, including reports of
32 child abuse, that meet the standards applicable under the laws of this State for all
33 other proposed adoptive placements;
34 (2) Uses the prevailing social and cultural standards of the Indian child’s
35 tribe as the standards for evaluation of the proposed adoptive placement;
36 (3) Includes an evaluation of the background, safety and health
37 information of the proposed adoptive placement, including the biological,
38 psychological and social factors of the proposed adoptive placement and
39 assessment of the commitment, capability and suitability of the proposed adoptive
40 placement to meet the Indian child’s needs; and
41 (4) Except where the proposed adoptive placement is in the Indian
42 child’s current foster care placement, is completed before the placement of the
43 Indian child in the proposed adoptive placement.
44 (c) Notwithstanding subsection 2, the court may not accept the tribe’s order
45 or judgment of tribal customary adoption if any adult living in the proposed
46 adoptive placement has a felony conviction for child abuse or neglect, spousal
47 abuse, crimes against a child, including, child pornography, or a crime involving
48 violence. The Division shall, by regulation, define “crime involving violence” for
49 the purpose of this paragraph. The definition must include rape, sexual assault
50 and homicide, but must not include other physical assault or battery.
51 2. The court shall accept an order or judgment for tribal customary
52 adoption that is filed by the Indian child’s tribe if:

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 27
1 (a) The court determines that tribal customary adoption is an appropriate
2 permanent placement option for the Indian child;
3 (b) The court finds that the tribal customary adoption is in the [Indian
4 child’s] best interest [,] of the child, as described in NRS 125E.230; and
5 (c) The order or judgment:
6 (1) Includes a description of the modification of the legal relationship of
7 the Indian child’s parents or Indian custodian and the Indian child, including
8 any contact between the Indian child and the Indian child’s parents or Indian
9 custodian, responsibilities of the Indian child’s parents or Indian custodian and
10 the rights of inheritance of the parents and Indian child;
11 (2) Includes a description of the Indian child’s legal relationship with the
12 tribe; and
13 (3) Does not include any child support obligations from the Indian
14 child’s parents or Indian custodian.
15  The court shall afford full faith and credit to a tribal customary adoption order
16 or judgment that is accepted under this subsection.
17 3. A tribal customary adoptive parent is not required to file a petition for
18 adoption when the court accepts a tribal customary adoption order or judgment
19 under subsection 2. The clerk of the court may not charge or collect a fee for a
20 proceeding under this subsection.
21 4. After accepting a tribal customary adoption order or judgment under
22 subsection 2, the court that accepted the order or judgment shall proceed as
23 provided in section 79 of this act and enter an order of adoption. In addition to
24 the requirements under section 80 of this act, the order of adoption must include
25 a statement that any parental rights or obligations not specified in the order are
26 transferred to the tribal customary adoptive parents and a description of any
27 parental rights or duties retained by the Indian child’s parents, the rights of
28 inheritance of the parents and the Indian child and the Indian child’s legal
29 relationship with the child’s tribe.
30 5. A tribal customary adoption under this section does not require the
31 consent of the Indian child or the child’s parents.
32 6. Upon the court’s entry of an order of adoption under this section, the
33 court’s jurisdiction over the Indian child terminates.
34 7. Any parental rights or obligations not specifically retained by the Indian
35 child’s parents in the order of adoption are conclusively presumed to transfer to
36 the tribal customary adoptive parents.
37 8. This section remains operative only to the extent that compliance with the

48 10. As used in this section, “tribal customary adoption” means the adoption
49 of an Indian child, by and through the tribal custom, traditions or law of the

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 28
1 Sec. 91. 1. The parent or parents and the prospective adoptive parent or
2 parents of a child to be adopted may enter into an enforceable agreement that
3 provides for postadoptive contact between:
4 (a) The child and the parent or parents;
5 (b) The adoptive parent or parents and the parent or parents; or
6 (c) Any combination thereof.
7 2. An agreement that provides for postadoptive contact is enforceable if:
8 (a) The agreement is in writing and signed by the parties;
9 (b) The agreement is incorporated into an order of adoption;
10 (c) The agreement is signed by a parent or parents before:
11 (1) The termination or voluntary relinquishment of the parental rights of
12 the parent or parents; or
13 (2) The execution of a specific consent to adoption or relinquishment;
14 and
15 (d) In the case of an agreement that concerns a child who was in the custody
16 of an agency which provides child welfare services before being adopted:
17 (1) The agency which provides child welfare services has determined that
18 the agreement is in the best interest of the child; or
19 (2) The court has determined, after a hearing, that the agreement is in
20 the best interest of the child.
21 3. The identity of a parent is not required to be included in an agreement
22 that provides for postadoptive contact. If such information is withheld, an agent
23 who may receive service of process for the parent must be provided in the
24 agreement.
25 4. A parent or adoptive parent who enters into an agreement that provides
26 for postadoptive contact shall include in the agreement an address at which the
27 parent or adoptive parent may receive service of a petition filed pursuant to
28 section 94 of this act unless the parent or adoptive parent elects to receive service
29 by alternate means through electronic mail rather than certified or registered
30 mail, in which case, the electronic mail address must be included in the
31 agreement. If a parent or adoptive parent refuses or fails to include such an
32 address in an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact, the court may, on
33 the date on which the court enters an order of adoption which incorporates the
34 agreement, order the agency which provides child welfare services to provide the
35 court with the contact information of the parent or adoptive parent who refused
36 or failed to include the address. If a court so orders, the court shall:
37 (a) Append the address to the agreement for postadoptive contact; and
38 (b) Make the address available to any party to the agreement who wishes to
39 file a petition pursuant to section 94 of this act.
40 5. If a parent or adoptive parent changes the address that was included in
41 an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact pursuant to subsection 4, the
42 parent shall file with the clerk of the court notice of the change of address within
43 15 days after the change of address.
44 6. A court that enters an order of adoption which incorporates an
45 agreement that provides for postadoptive contact shall retain jurisdiction to
46 enforce, modify or terminate the agreement that provides for postadoptive contact
47 until:
48 (a) The child reaches 18 years of age;
49 (b) The child becomes emancipated; or
50 (c) The agreement is terminated.
51 7. The establishment of an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact
52 does not affect the rights of an adoptive parent as the legal parent of the child as
53 set forth in section 38 of this act.

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 29

51 (a) During the period set forth in subsection 2 of section 95 of this act,
52 petition the court that entered the order of adoption of the child to enforce the

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 30
1 terms of the agreement that provides for postadoptive contact if the agreement
2 complies with the requirements of subsection 2 of section 91 of this act; and
3 (b) Petition the court that entered the order of adoption of the child to modify
4 or terminate the agreement that provides for postadoptive contact in the manner
5 set forth in section 96 of this act.
6 3. A petition filed pursuant to this section must be:
7 (a) Filed under the same case number as the proceeding for adoption;
8 (b) Served by the parent or adoptive parent who filed the petition using
9 certified or registered mail with return receipt requested, or if elected by any of
10 the parties to the postadoptive contact agreement to receive service by alternate
11 means through electronic mail, upon each other parent or adoptive parent, as
12 applicable, who has entered into the agreement that provides for postadoptive
13 contact at the address provided pursuant to subsection 4 or 5 of section 91 of this
14 act; and
15 (c) Heard by:
16 (1) If available, the judge who issued the order of adoption of the child;
17 (2) If the judge described in subparagraph (1) is unavailable and if a
18 family court has been established in the judicial district, a judge of the family
19 court; or
20 (3) If the judge described in subparagraph (1) is unavailable and if a
21 family court has not been established in the judicial district, any district judge of
22 the judicial district.
23 Sec. 95. 1. Failure to comply with the terms of an agreement that
24 provides for postadoptive contact entered into pursuant to section 91 of this act
25 may not be used as a ground to:
26 (a) Set aside an order of adoption;
27 (b) Revoke, nullify or set aside a valid specific consent to adoption or
28 relinquishment; or
29 (c) Except as otherwise provided in NRS 41.509, award any civil damages to
30 a party to the agreement.
31 2. Any action to enforce the terms of an agreement that provides for
32 postadoptive contact must be commenced not later than 120 days after the date on
33 which the agreement was breached.
34 Sec. 96. 1. An agreement that provides for postadoptive contact entered
35 into pursuant to section 91 of this act may only be modified or terminated by an
36 adoptive parent petitioning the court that entered the order which included the
37 agreement. The court may grant a request to modify or terminate the agreement
38 only if:
39 (a) The adoptive parent petitioning the court for the modification or
40 termination establishes that:
41 (1) A change in circumstances warrants the modification or termination;
42 and
43 (2) The contact provided for in the agreement is no longer in the best
44 interest of the child; or
45 (b) Each party to the agreement consents to the modification or termination.
46 2. If an adoptive parent petitions the court for a modification or termination
47 of an agreement pursuant to this section:
48 (a) There is a presumption that the modification or termination is in the best
49 interest of the child; and
50 (b) The court may consider the wishes of the child involved in the agreement.
51 3. Any order issued pursuant to this section to modify an agreement that
52 provides for postadoptive contact:

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 31
1 (a) May limit, restrict, condition or decrease contact between the parties
2 involved in the agreement; and
3 (b) May not expand or increase the contact between the parties involved in
4 the agreement or place any new obligation on an adoptive parent.
5 Sec. 97. As used in sections 97 to 105, inclusive, of this act, unless the
6 context otherwise requires, “person” includes a hospital.
7 Sec. 98. 1. The Division shall:
8 (a) Establish reasonable minimum standards for child-placing agencies.
9 (b) In consultation with each agency which provides child welfare services,
10 adopt:
11 (1) Regulations concerning the operation of an agency which provides
12 child welfare services.
13 (2) Regulations establishing the procedure to be used by an agency
14 which provides child welfare services in placing children for adoption, which
15 must allow the parent or parents and the prospective adoptive parent or parents to
16 determine, by mutual agreement, the amount of identifying information that will
17 be communicated concerning each of them.
18 (3) Any other regulations necessary to carry out its powers and duties
19 regarding the adoption of children or the placement of children for adoption,
20 including, without limitation, such regulations necessary to ensure compliance
21 with the provisions of this chapter and any regulations adopted pursuant thereto.
22 2. Each agency which provides child welfare services shall conform to the
23 standards established and the regulations adopted pursuant to subsection 1.
24 Sec. 99. 1. Except as otherwise provided in this section:
25 (a) In a county whose population is less than 100,000, the Division shall, in
26 accordance with NRS 432.014; and
27 (b) In a county whose population is 100,000 or more, the board of the county
28 commissioners of the county shall, by ordinance,
29  charge reasonable fees for the services provided by an agency which provides
30 child welfare services in placing, arranging the placement of or assisting in the
31 placing or arranging the placement of any child for adoption and for conducting
32 any investigation required by section 100 of this act.
33 2. The fees charged for those services must vary based on criteria developed
34 by the Division and board of county commissioners but must not exceed the usual
35 and customary fees that child-placing agencies in the area where the services
36 provided, or in a similar geographic area, would charge for those services. The
37 Division and board of county commissioners shall not discriminate between
38 adoptions made through an agency and specific adoptions in setting their fees.
39 3. A fee must not be charged for services related to adoption of a child with
40 special needs.
41 4. An agency which provides child welfare services may waive or reduce
42 any fee charged pursuant to this section if the agency which provides child
43 welfare services determines that the adoptive parents are not able to pay the fee or
44 the needs of the child require a waiver or reduction of the fee.
45 5. Any money collected by an agency which provides child welfare services
46 in a county whose population is less than 100,000 pursuant to this section must
47 be accounted for in the appropriate account of the Division and may be used only
48 to pay for the costs of any adoptive or postadoptive services provided by any
49 agency which provides child welfare services in a county whose population is less
50 than 100,000.
51 6. Any money collected by an agency which provides child welfare services
52 in a county whose population is 100,000 or more pursuant to this section must be
53 deposited in the county treasury for the credit of the agency which provides child

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 32
1 welfare services and may be used only to pay for the costs of any adoption or
2 postadoptive services provided by the agency which provides child welfare
3 services.
4 Sec. 100. 1. The agency which provides child welfare services shall
5 complete a home study that investigates the medical, mental, financial and moral
6 backgrounds of the prospective adoptive parents to determine the suitability of the
7 home for placement of the child for adoption. The investigation must also
8 embrace any other relevant factor relating to the qualifications of the prospective
9 adoptive parent or parents.
10 2. If the placement is to be made in a home outside of this State, the agency
11 which provides child welfare services must receive a copy of a report, completed
12 by the appropriate authority, of an investigation of the home and the medical,
13 mental, financial and moral backgrounds of the prospective adoptive parent or
14 parents to determine the suitability of the home for placement of the child for
15 adoption.
16 Sec. 101. 1. A prospective adoptive parent who is subject to a home study
17 by the agency which provides child welfare services must submit as part of the
18 investigation a complete set of fingerprints and written permission authorizing
19 the agency which provides child welfare services to forward those fingerprints to
20 the Central Repository for Nevada Records of Criminal History for submission to
21 the Federal Bureau of Investigation.
22 2. The agency which provides child welfare services may exchange with the
23 Central Repository or the Federal Bureau of Investigation any information
24 respecting the fingerprints submitted.
25 3. When a report from the Federal Bureau of Investigation is received by
26 the Central Repository, it shall immediately forward a copy of the report to the
27 agency which provides child welfare services that submitted the fingerprints.
28 4. Any fees for fingerprinting and submission to the Central Repository and
29 the Federal Bureau of Investigation must be paid by the prospective adoptive
30 parent, except that:
31 (a) In a county whose population is less than 100,000, the Division may
32 adopt regulations providing for the payment of those fees by the Division; or
33 (b) In a county whose population is 100,000 or more, the board of county
34 commissioners may provide by ordinance for the payment of those fees by the
35 agency which provides child welfare services.
36 Sec. 102. 1. The Division, in consultation with each agency which
37 provides child welfare services, shall adopt regulations setting forth the criteria to
38 be used by an agency which provides child welfare services for determining
39 whether a prospective adoptive home is suitable or unsuitable for the placement
40 of a child for adoption.
41 2. Upon the completion of a home study conducted by an agency which
42 provides child welfare services pursuant to section 100 of this act, the agency
43 which provides child welfare services shall inform the prospective adoptive parent
44 or parents of the results of the home study. If, pursuant to the home study, a
45 determination is made that a prospective adoptive home is unsuitable for
46 placement or detrimental to the interest of the child, the agency which provides
47 child welfare services shall provide the prospective adoptive parent or parents
48 with an opportunity to review and respond to the home study with the agency
49 which provides child welfare services before the issuance of the results of the
50 home study. Except as otherwise provided in NRS 239.0115, the identity of those
51 persons who are interviewed or submit information concerning the home study
52 must remain confidential.

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 33
1 3. An agency which provides child welfare services shall not determine that
2 a prospective adoptive home is unsuitable for placement or detrimental to the
3 interest of the child solely because the prospective adoptive parent or parents:
4 (a) Are deaf, are blind or have another physical disability; or
5 (b) Are the holders of a valid registry identification card.
6 Sec. 103. 1. Whenever the agency which provides child welfare services
7 believes that anyone has violated or is about to violate any of the provisions of
8 this chapter, in addition to any other penalty or remedy provided:
9 (a) The agency which provides child welfare services may petition the
10 appropriate district court for an order to restrain and enjoin the violation or
11 threatened violation of any of the provisions of this chapter, or to compel
12 compliance with the provisions of this chapter; and
13 (b) The court shall, if a child has been or was about to be placed in a
14 prospective adoptive home in violation of the provisions of this chapter [prohibit]
15 :
16 (1) Prohibit the placement if the child was about to be so placed ; [,] or
17 [order]
18 (2) Order the removal of the child if the child was so placed within 6
19 months before the filing of the petition by the agency which provides child
20 welfare services [.] and the court determines that it is in the best interest of the
21 child for the child to be removed from the prospective adoptive home.
22 2. Whenever the agency which provides child welfare services believes that
23 a person has received for the purpose of adoption a child not related by blood,
24 and the required written notice has not been given, if the agency which provides
25 child welfare services does not proceed pursuant to subsection 1, it shall make an
26 investigation. Upon completion of the investigation, if the home is found suitable
27 for the child, the prospective adoptive parents must be allowed 6 months from the
28 date of completion of the investigation to file a petition for adoption. If a petition
29 for adoption is not filed within that time a license as a foster home must
30 thereafter be issued pursuant to NRS 424.030 if the home meets the established
31 standards. If, in the opinion of the agency which provides child welfare services,
32 the placement is detrimental to the interest of the child, the agency which
33 provides child welfare services shall file an application with the district court for
34 an order for the removal of the child from the home.
35 Sec. 104. An agency which provides child welfare services shall, to the
36 extent practicable, give preference to the placement of a child for adoption
37 together with the siblings of the child.
38 Sec. 105. 1. If a child who is in the custody of an agency which provides
39 child welfare services is placed for adoption, the agency must provide the court
40 which is conducting the adoption proceedings with a copy of any order for
41 visitation with a sibling of the child that was issued pursuant to NRS 432B.580.
42 2. The court shall incorporate an order for visitation provided to the court
43 pursuant to subsection 1 into the order of adoption unless, not later than 30 days
44 after notice of the filing of the petition for adoption is provided to all legal
45 custodians or guardians of the child who are required to be provided with such
46 notice pursuant to section 76 of this act, any interested party in the adoption,
47 including, without limitation, the prospective adoptive parent, the adoptive child,
48 a sibling of the adoptive child, the agency which provides child welfare services
49 petitions the court to exclude the order of visitation with a sibling from the order
50 of adoption or amend the order for visitation before including the order in the
51 order of adoption.
52 3. The hearing on a petition submitted pursuant to subsection 2 must be
53 held on the same date as the hearing on the petition for adoption. Any interested

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 34
1 party is entitled to participate in the hearing. The clerk of the court shall give
2 written notice of the time and place of the hearing to the prospective adoptive
3 parent, the adoptive child, a sibling of the adoptive child, the attorney for the
4 adoptive child or a sibling of the adoptive child and the agency which provides
5 child welfare services. Upon the petition of a sibling requesting the inclusion of
6 an order for visitation in the order of adoption, the court may require the agency
7 which provides child welfare services to provide the clerk of the court with the
8 contact information of the prospective adoptive parent, the adoptive child and the
9 attorney for the adoptive child. If so ordered, the agency which provides child
10 welfare services must provide such contact information under seal.
11 4. The sole consideration of the court in making a determination
12 concerning visitation with a sibling pursuant to this section is the best interest of
13 the child. If a petition is submitted pursuant to subsection 2, the court must not
14 enter an order of adoption until the court has made a determination concerning
15 visitation with a sibling.
16 5. If an order for visitation with a sibling is included in an order of
17 adoption, the court shall, upon the request of a party to the order, provide to the
18 party the case number of the adoption proceeding and any documents or records
19 necessary to enforce, modify or terminate the order.
20 6. A party to an order for visitation may petition for enforcement of the
21 order at any time while the order is in effect. A person who fails to comply with
22 the order is in contempt of court. If a party to an order for visitation withholds
23 the contact information of any person in violation of the order, the court may
24 order the agency which provides child welfare services to provide such contact
25 information to the court under seal.
26 Sec. 106. Title 11 of NRS is hereby amended by adding thereto a new

29 Sec. 107. In addition to any requirement set forth in sections 2 to 46,
30 inclusive, of this act, as applicable:
31 1. The provisions of sections 108 to 111, inclusive, and 114 of this act
32 govern confirmatory adoptions.
33 2. The provisions of sections 112, 113 and 114 of this act govern
34 readoptions.
35 Sec. 108. A petition for a confirmatory adoption must include:
36 1. Any information required by NRS 127.110; and
37 2. A statement of how parentage has already been established.
38 Sec. 109. 1. A copy of one of the following must be placed in the record of
39 the confirmatory adoption:
40 (a) The birth certificate of the child listing the prospective adoptive parent as
41 a parent of the child;
42 (b) A court order establishing parentage of the child; or
43 (c) Any other evidence that is deemed sufficient by the court to establish
44 parentage of the child.
45 2. A document or other evidence described in subsection 1 is confidential.
46 Sec. 110. An order of confirmatory adoption must confirm:
47 1. Each legal parent of the child; and
48 2. The new name of the child, if requested in the petition pursuant to
49 section [109] 108 of this act.
50 Sec. 111. A confirmatory adoption may be sought in this State if the birth
51 certificate of the child was issued in this State.

1 Sec. 112. 1. A petitioner and any spouse of the petitioner who adopts a
2 child through an intercountry adoption may petition to readopt the child in this
3 State.
4 2. As used in this section, “intercountry adoption” means the process by
5 which a person adopts a child in another country by permanent legal means and
6 brings the child back to live permanently with the person.

15 Sec. 114. 1. After an order of confirmatory adoption or readoption has
16 been entered, the court shall direct the petitioner or the attorney of the petitioner
17 to prepare a report of adoption on a form prescribed and furnished by the State
18 Registrar of Vital Statistics or the equivalent office in the state that issued the
19 birth certificate. The report may:
20 (a) Identify the original certificate of birth of the person adopted;
21 (b) Provide sufficient information to prepare a new certificate of birth for the
22 person adopted;
23 (c) Identify the order of adoption; and
24 (d) Be certified by the clerk of the court.

26 attorney of the petitioner shall prepare a report to the State Registrar of Vital
27 Statistics, which includes sufficient information to identify the original order of
28 adoption and the provisions of that order which were amended or annulled.
29 Sec. 115. Title 11 of NRS is hereby amended by adding thereto a new
30 chapter to consist of the provisions set forth as sections 116 to 153, inclusive, of
31 this act.
32 Sec. 116. As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise requires, the
33 words and terms defined in section 117 to 121, inclusive, of this act, have the
34 meanings ascribed to them in those sections.
35 Sec. 117. “Parent” means a person:
36 1. Who has legal rights, privileges, responsibilities and obligations to a
37 child and is a biological or legal parent of a child whose parental rights have not
38 been terminated by a court order or execution of a specific consent to adoption or
39 relinquishment;
40 2. Who is a putative parent or proven parent of a child;
41 3. Who is presumed to be the parent of a child;
42 4. Whose paternity or parentage has been established pursuant to chapter
43 126 of NRS; or
44 5. Whose parentage has been confirmed by a court order.
45 Sec. 118. “Placing parent” means a parent who executed a specific consent
46 to adoption or relinquishment pursuant to this chapter.
47 Sec. 119. “Prospective adoptive parent” means a person with whom a child
48 has been placed for adoption but whose petition for adoption has not been
49 granted by the court.
50 Sec. 120. “Relinquishment” means a document that is executed in an
51 adoption which:
52 1. Terminates the parental rights of the person executing the document in
53 the child to be adopted; and

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 36
1 2. Places the child for adoption with a named child-placing agency.
2 Sec. 121. “Specific consent to adoption” means a document that is
3 executed in an identified adoption which:
4 1. Terminates or retains the parental right of the person executing the
5 document; and
6 2. Authorizes the child to be adopted by a specifically named person or
7 persons.
8 Sec. 122. In addition to the requirements set forth in the chapter consisting
9 of sections 2 to 46, inclusive, of this act, as applicable, this chapter governs close-
10 family adoptions.
11 Sec. 123. 1. Except as otherwise provided in chapter 125E of NRS and
12 sections 127, 140, 144, 145 and 146 of this act, a child of whom this State:
13 (a) Is the home state on the date of the commencement of the proceeding; or
14 (b) Was the home state within 6 months before the commencement of the
15 proceeding,
16  may not be adopted except upon an order of a district court in this State.
17 2. As used in this section, “home state” means:
18 (a) The state in which a child lived for at least 6 consecutive months,
19 including any temporary absence from the state, such as a placement outside of
20 the state through the Interstate Compact on the Placement of Children pursuant
21 to NRS 127.320 to 127.350, inclusive, immediately before the commencement of a
22 proceeding; or
23 (b) In the case of a child less than 6 months of age, the state in which the
24 child lived from birth, including any temporary absence from the state.
25 Sec. 124. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 2:
26 (a) A child may be adopted by one or more adults subject to the rules
27 prescribed in this chapter;
28 (b) A person adopting a child must be at least 10 years older than the person
29 adopted; and
30 (c) If the child is over the age of 14 years, the child must agree to the
31 adoption.
32 2. A court may approve the adoption of a child without regard to the age
33 difference of the child and the prospective adoptive parents if the court is satisfied
34 that it is in the best interest of the child.
35 Sec. 124.5. Compliance with the requirements of the Interstate Compact on
36 the Placement of Children pursuant to NRS 127.320 to 127.350, inclusive, may be
37 performed by an agency which provides child welfare services, a child-placing
38 agency or an attorney licensed to practice law in this State.
39 Sec. 125. 1. One or more adults may petition the district court of any
40 county in this State for leave to adopt a child. Each prospective adoptive parent
41 and each agreeing parent seeking to retain parental rights must be a joint
42 petitioner and agree to the adoption.
43 2. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 5, a married person not
44 lawfully separated from a spouse may not adopt a child without the agreement of
45 the spouse, if such spouse is capable of giving such agreement to the adoption.
46 3. If a spouse agrees to an adoption as described in subsection 2, such
47 agreement does not establish any parental rights or responsibilities on the part of
48 the spouse unless the spouse:
49 (a) Has, in a writing filed with the court, [specifically] agreed to:
50 (1) Adopting the child; and
51 (2) Establishing parental rights and responsibilities; and
52 (b) Is named as an adoptive parent in the order of adoption.

1 4. The court shall not name a spouse who agrees to an adoption as

14 Sec. 126. Except as otherwise provided in section 135 of this act, a specific
15 consent to adoption or a relinquishment is required from:
16 1. Each parent of the child who is alive; and
17 2. Any legal guardian of the person of the child appointed by a court of

19 Sec. 127. 1. If a petition for adoption of a child concerns the adoption of
20 an Indian child, unless the parental rights of the Indian child’s parents have
21 been terminated, consent in writing to the adoption must be given by the Indian
22 child’s parents. Such written consent must be filed with the court.
23 2. An Indian child’s parent may consent to the adoption of the Indian child
24 at any time not less than 10 days following the date of the Indian child’s birth by
25 executing the consent in person before the court on the record.
26 3. Before the execution of a parent’s consent under subsection 2, the court
27 must explain to the parent on the record in detail and in the language of the
28 parent:
29 (a) The right to legal counsel;
30 (b) The terms and consequences of the consent in detail; and
31 (c) That at any time before the entry of the order of adoption, the parent may
32 withdraw consent for any reason and petition the court to have the child
33 returned.
34 4. After the execution of a parent’s consent under subsection 2, the court
35 shall certify that the court made the explanation under subsection 3 and that the
36 parent fully understood the explanation.
37 5. At any time before the entry of an order of adoption, an Indian child’s
38 parent may withdraw the parent’s consent under this section. The withdrawal of
39 consent must be made by filing the written withdrawal with the court or by
40 making a statement of withdrawal on the record in the adoption proceeding.
41 Upon entry of the withdrawal of consent, the court must promptly notify the
42 person or entity that arranged the adoptive placement to regain custody and
43 control of the Indian child. A parent who withdraws consent may petition the
44 court for the return of the child.
45 6. As used in this section, “parent” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS
46 125E.130.

14 Sec. 129. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 2, a specific
