25 Sec. 132. If a person to whom a specific consent to adopt a child is given
26 for an adoption pursuant to section 129 of this act has, at the time the specific
27 consent is executed, legal custody over the child, the person is legally responsible
28 for the child and shall provide for the care, support and maintenance of the child
29 until a court holds a hearing to enter an order of adoption or to deny the petition
30 pursuant to the laws of this State or another state.
31 Sec. 133. 1. If a prospective adoptive parent or parents determine that an
32 adoption cannot or should not proceed, the adoptive parent or parents, as
33 applicable, may:
34 (a) Withdraw a petition for termination of parental rights or a petition for
35 adoption; and
36 (b) Declare the specific consent to adoption void and surrender the adoptive
37 placement.
38 2. The declaration surrendering the adoptive placement pursuant to
39 subsection 1 must:
40 (a) Be in writing, notarized and acknowledged by the surrendering
41 prospective adoptive parent or parents; and
42 (b) Give notice to [all] :
43 (1) All parents of the child [, the] ;
44 (2) The court of competent jurisdiction , if a petition for adoption has
45 been filed; and [the]
46 (3) The child-placing agency, if applicable.
47 3. If a prospective adoptive parent or parents makes a declaration
48 surrendering an adoptive placement pursuant to subsection 1 [, the] :
49 (a) The prospective adoptive parent or parents must return the child to the
50 placing parent or parents, if the placing parent or parents wish to accept and
51 regain custody of the child [.] ; or

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 41
1 (b) If the placing parent or parents decline to accept the child, the placing
2 parent or parents may relinquish the child to a child-placing agency for
3 placement.
4 4. A specific consent to adoption or relinquishment declared void is without
5 legal effect and the parental rights are restored.
6 5. An adoptive placement may not be surrendered after an order finalizing
7 the adoption has been entered by the court.
8 Sec. 134. 1. All specific consents to adoption and relinquishments
9 executed in this State by the parent who gave birth to a child before the birth of
10 the child or within 72 hours after the birth of the child are invalid.
11 2. A specific consent to adoption or relinquishment may be executed by a
12 parent who does not give birth to the child before the birth of a child if the parent
13 is not married to the parent who gave birth to the child.
14 3. A minor parent may execute a specific consent to adoption or
15 relinquishment without notifying or obtaining the consent of the parent or
16 parents of the minor.
17 4. A specific consent to adoption or relinquishment cannot be revoked or
18 nullified by the executing parent.
19 5. A specific consent to adoption or relinquishment executed by a minor
20 parent cannot be revoked or nullified based upon the minor parent becoming an
21 adult.
22 6. A specific consent to adoption or relinquishment can become invalid if:
23 (a) Every parent of the child does not execute a specific consent to adoption
24 of the child or relinquishment or have his or her parental rights terminated by a
25 court of competent jurisdiction within 18 months after the execution of the
26 specific consent to adoption or relinquishment;
27 (b) No petition for adoption of the child has been filed by the person or
28 persons named in the specific consent to adoption within 18 months after the
29 execution of the specific consent to adoption or relinquishment;
30 (c) The specific consent to adoption or relinquishment is declared void
31 pursuant to section 133 of this act; or
32 (d) The specific consent to adoption or relinquishment was obtained under
33 fraud, duress or undue influence and the action to void the specific consent to
34 adoption or relinquishment is brought not later than 30 days after the execution.
35 Sec. 135. The execution of a specific consent to adoption or relinquishment
36 by a parent shall not be necessary:
37 1. Where parental rights have been terminated by an order of a court of
38 competent jurisdiction;
39 2. Upon the death of the parent, as evidenced by a certificate of death or
40 other evidence deemed sufficient by the court; or
41 3. Upon the termination of the parental rights of the parent through
42 operation of law by a birth father registry operated in another state.
43 Sec. 136. 1. A petition for adoption of a child may be filed at any time
44 after placement with the petitioners.
45 2. The petition for adoption must state, in substance, the following:
46 (a) The full name and age of the petitioners.
47 (b) The age of the child sought to be adopted and the date that the child was
48 placed with the petitioners.
49 (c) That it is the desire of the petitioners that the relationship of parent and
50 child be established between them and the child.
51 (d) If the petitioners desire to change the name of the child, the new name
52 desired.

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 42
1 (e) That the petitioners are fit and proper persons to have the care and
2 custody of the child.
3 (f) That they are financially able to provide for the child.
4 (g) That there has been a full compliance with the law in regard to the
5 termination of parental rights, specific consent to adoption [.] or relinquishment
6 as to all parents.
7 (h) Whether the petitioners have reason to know that the child is an Indian
8 child.
9 (i) That there are no known signs that the child is currently experiencing
10 victimization from human trafficking, exploitation or abuse.
11 (j) Whether an agreement for postadoptive contact has been entered into by
12 the parent or parents of the child and the prospective adoptive parent or parents
13 of the child.
14 (k) Whether there is an order for visitation of a child by a sibling or other
15 relative.
16 Sec. 137. Notice of the filing of a petition for the adoption of a child must
17 be provided to all legal custodians or guardians of the child who are not a parent
18 of the child.
19 Sec. 138. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 2, the prospective
20 adoptive parent or parents, child to be adopted, representative of the child-placing
21 agency and counsel for the parties may attend by telephone or [video] remote
22 appearance in lieu of attending in person, any hearings held by the court
23 concerning the petition for adoption.
24 2. The court may waive the attendance of a child to be adopted for good
25 cause shown.
26 Sec. 139. If the court finds that the best interest of the child warrants the
27 granting of the petition, an order of adoption must be made and filed, ordering
28 that henceforth the child is the child of the petitioners. When determining
29 whether the best interest of the child warrants the granting of a petition that is
30 filed by a prospective adoptive parent, the court shall give strong consideration to
31 the emotional bond between the child and the prospective adoptive parent. In the
32 order the court may change the name of the child, if desired.
33 Sec. 140. 1. An order entered pursuant to 139 of this act must include:
34 (a) A finding that the petitioner complied with the inquiry requirements
35 under subsection 1 of NRS 125E.210 to determine whether there is reason to
36 know that the child is an Indian child; and
37 (b) A finding that the child is or is not an Indian child.
38 2. In an adoption of an Indian child, the order must include:
39 (a) The birth name and date of birth of the Indian child, the Indian child’s
40 tribal affiliation and the name of the Indian child after adoption;
41 (b) If known, the names and addresses of the parents;
42 (c) The names and addresses of the adoptive parents;
43 (d) The name and contact information for any agency having files or
44 information relating to the adoption;
45 (e) Any information relating to tribal membership or eligibility for tribal
46 membership of the Indian child;
47 (f) The determination regarding the Indian child’s residence, domicile and
48 tribal wardship status as required under NRS 125E.250;
49 (g) A finding that the petitioner complied with the notice requirements under
50 subsection 2 of NRS 125E.220;
51 (h) If the adoptive placement and the parents entered into a post-adoptive
52 contact agreement or the adoptive placement and the Indian child’s tribe has
53 entered into an agreement that requires the adoptive placement to maintain

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 43
1 connection between the child and the child’s tribe, the terms of the agreement;
2 and
3 (i) A finding that the adoptive placement complies with the placement
4 preferences under NRS 125E.350 or, if the placement does not comply with the
5 placement preferences under NRS 125E.350, a finding upon the petitioner’s
6 motion under subsection 3 of NRS 125E.350 that good cause exists for placement
7 contrary to the placement preferences.
8 3. For each finding or determination made under this section, the court
9 must provide a description of the facts upon which the finding or determination is
10 based.
11 4. Upon entry of the order of adoption of an Indian child, the court shall
12 provide to the United States Bureau of Indian Affairs copies of the order entered
13 pursuant to section 139 of this act, any affidavit signed by a consenting parent
14 requesting anonymity, and all other required information in accordance with 25
15 C.F.R. § 23.140.
16 Sec. 141. 1. After an order of adoption has been entered, the court shall
17 direct the petitioner or the attorney of the petitioner to prepare a report of
18 adoption on a form prescribed and furnished by the State Registrar of Vital
19 Statistics or the equivalent office in the state that issued the birth certificate. The
20 report may:
21 (a) Identify the original certificate of birth of the person adopted;
22 (b) Provide sufficient information to prepare a new certificate of birth for the
23 person adopted;
24 (c) Identify the order of adoption; and
25 (d) Be certified by the clerk of the court.
26 2. If an order of adoption is amended or annulled, the petitioner or the
27 attorney of the petitioner shall prepare a report to the State Registrar of Vital
28 Statistics, which includes sufficient information to identify the original order of
29 adoption and the provisions of that order which were amended or annulled.
30 Sec. 142. 1. A placing parent of a child may not bring an action to set
31 aside an adoption after a petition for adoption has been granted, unless a court of
32 competent jurisdiction has previously, in a separate action:
33 (a) Set aside the specific consent to adoption;
34 (b) Set aside the relinquishment of the child for adoption; or
35 (c) Reversed an order terminating the parental rights of the placing parent.
36 2. After a petition for adoption has been granted, there is a presumption for
37 the purposes of this chapter that remaining in the home of the adoptive parents is
38 in the best interest of the child.
39 Sec. 143. 1. The child-placing agency may consent to the adoption of a
40 child under 18 years of age with special needs due to race, age or physical or
41 mental problems who is in the custody of the child-placing agency by [proposed]
42 prospective adoptive parents when, in the judgment of the child-placing agency, it
43 would be in the best interest of the child to be placed in that adoptive home.
44 2. The child-placing agency shall in a timely and diligent manner:
45 (a) Schedule any evaluations necessary to identify any special needs the child
46 may have.
47 (b) If it determines that the child has any special needs:
48 (1) Notify the prospective adoptive parents:
49 (I) That they may be eligible for a grant of financial assistance
50 pursuant to this section; and
51 (II) The manner in which to apply for such financial assistance; and
52 (2) Assist the prospective adoptive parents in applying for and satisfying
53 any other prerequisites necessary to obtain a grant of financial assistance

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 44
1 pursuant to this section and any other relevant subsidies and services which may
2 be available.
3 3. All financial assistance provided under this section ceases immediately
4 when the child:
5 (a) Reaches 18 years of age, if the child is not enrolled in school, or 19 years
6 of age, if the child is enrolled in school;
7 (b) Graduates from high school, if the child is at least 18 years of age;
8 (c) Becomes self-supporting;
9 (d) Is emancipated; or
10 (e) Dies.
11 4. Neither a grant of financial assistance pursuant to this section nor any
12 discontinuance of such assistance affects the legal status or respective obligations
13 of any party to the adoption.
14 5. A court shall waive all court costs of the [proposed] prospective adoptive
15 parents in an adoption proceeding for a child with special needs if the child-
16 placing agency consents to the adoption of such a child pursuant to this section.
17 6. The Division, in consultation with each agency which provides child
18 welfare services, shall adopt regulations regarding eligibility for and the
19 procedures for applying for a grant of financial assistance pursuant to this
20 section.
21 Sec. 144. 1. A petition to vacate an order of adoption of an Indian child
22 under this chapter may be filed in a court of competent jurisdiction by a parent
23 who consented to the adoption.
24 2. Upon the filing of a petition under this section, the court shall set a time
25 for a hearing on the petition and provide notice of the petition and hearing to
26 each party to the adoption proceeding and to the Indian child’s tribe.
27 3. After a hearing on the petition, the court shall vacate the order of
28 adoption if:
29 (a) The petition is filed not later than 2 years following the date of the order;
30 and
31 (b) The court finds by clear and convincing evidence that the parent’s
32 consent was obtained through fraud or duress.
33 4. When the court vacates an order of adoption under this section, the court
34 shall also order that the parental rights of the parent whose consent the court
35 found was obtained through fraud or duress be restored. The order restoring
36 parental rights under this section must include a plan for the physical custody of
37 the Indian child, whether the Indian child will be placed with an agency which
38 provides child welfare services or with the parent.
39 Sec. 145. 1. If an order of adoption of an Indian child under this chapter
40 is vacated, the court vacating the order must notify, by registered or certified mail
41 with return receipt requested, the Indian child’s former parents, prior Indian
42 custodian, if any, and Indian tribe and the appropriate child-placing agency.
43 2. The notice required under subsection 1 must:
44 (a) Include the Indian child’s current name and any former names as
45 reflected in the court record;
46 (b) Inform the recipient of the right to move the court for the return of
47 custody of and restoration of parental rights to the Indian child, if appropriate,
48 under this section;
49 (c) Provide sufficient information to allow the recipient to participate in any
50 scheduled hearings; and
51 (d) Be sent to the last known address in the court record.
52 3. An Indian child’s former parent or prior Indian custodian may waive
53 notice under this section by executing a waiver of notice in person before the

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 45
1 court and filing the waiver with the court. The waiver must clearly set out any
2 conditions to the waiver. Before the execution of the waiver, the court must
3 explain to the former parent or prior Indian custodian, on the record in detail
4 and in the language of the former parent or prior Indian custodian:
5 (a) The former parent’s right to legal counsel, if applicable;
6 (b) The terms and consequences of the waiver; and
7 (c) How the waiver may be revoked.
8 4. After execution of the waiver pursuant to subsection 3, the court shall
9 certify that it provided the explanation as required under subsection 3 and that
10 the former parent or prior Indian custodian fully understood the explanation.
11 5. At any time before the entry of an order of adoption of an Indian child,
12 the former parent or prior Indian custodian may revoke a waiver executed by the
13 former parent or prior Indian custodian pursuant to subsection 3 by filing a
14 written revocation with the court or by making a statement of revocation on the
15 record in a proceeding for the adoption of the Indian child.
16 6. If an order of adoption of an Indian child under this chapter is vacated
17 other than as provided in NRS 125E.360, an Indian child’s former parent or
18 prior Indian custodian may intervene in the proceeding and move the court for
19 the Indian child to be returned to the custody of the former parent or prior Indian
20 custodian and for the parental rights to the Indian child to be restored. The
21 moving party shall provide by registered or certified mail, return receipt
22 requested, notice of the motion for the Indian child to be returned to the custody
23 of the former parent or prior Indian custodian and the time set for filing
24 objections to the motion, together with notice of proceeding in the form required
25 under subsection 3 of NRS 125E.220 to:
26 (a) The agency which provides child welfare services in the county in which
27 the order was vacated;
28 (b) Each tribe of which the child may be a member or in which the Indian
29 child may be eligible for membership;
30 (c) The child’s parents;
31 (d) The child’s Indian custodian, if applicable; and
32 (e) The appropriate Regional Director of the United States Bureau of Indian
33 Affairs listed in 25 C.F.R. § 23.11(b), if the identity or location of the child’s
34 parents cannot be ascertained.
35  The petitioner shall file a declaration of compliance, including a copy of each
36 notice sent under this subsection, together with any return receipts or other proof
37 of service.
38 7. Upon the filing of an objection to a motion made pursuant to subsection
39 6, the court shall fix the time for hearing on objections.
40 8. The court shall order the Indian child to be returned to the custody of the
41 former parent or prior Indian custodian or restore the parental rights to the
42 Indian child unless the court finds, by clear and convincing evidence, that the
43 return of custody or restoration of parental rights is not in the [child’s] best
44 [interests,] interest of the child, as described in NRS 125E.230. If the court orders
45 the Indian child to be returned to the custody of the former parent or prior Indian
46 custodian, the court’s order must include a transition plan for the physical
47 custody of the child, which may include protective supervision.
48 9. As used in this section:
49 (a) “Former parent” means a person who was previously the parent of an
50 Indian child subject to an order of adoption under this chapter and whose
51 parental rights have not been restored under section 144 of this act.

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 46
1 (b) “Prior Indian custodian” means a person who was previously the
2 custodian of an Indian child subject to an order of adoption of the child under
3 this chapter.
4 Sec. 146. 1. Notwithstanding any other provision of law, if an Indian
5 child’s tribe or the United States Secretary of the Interior requests access to the
6 adoption records of an Indian child, the court must make the records available
7 not later than 14 days following the date of the request.
8 2. The records made available under subsection 1 must, at a minimum,
9 include the petition, all substantive orders entered in the adoption proceedings,
10 the complete record of the placement finding and, if the placement departs from
11 the placement preference under NRS 125E.350, detailed documentation of the
12 efforts to comply with the placement preferences.
13 Sec. 147. 1. The parent or parents and the prospective adoptive parent or
14 parents of a child to be adopted may enter into an enforceable agreement that
15 provides for postadoptive contact between:
16 (a) The child and the parent or parents;
17 (b) The adoptive parent or parents and the parent or parents; or
18 (c) Any combination thereof.
19 2. An agreement that provides for postadoptive contact is enforceable if:
20 (a) The agreement is in writing and signed by the parties;
21 (b) The agreement is incorporated into an order of adoption; and
22 (c) The agreement is signed by the parent or parents before:
23 (1) The termination or voluntary relinquishment of the parental rights of
24 the parent or parents; or
25 (2) The execution of a specific consent to adoption or relinquishment.
26 3. The identity of a parent is not required to be included in an agreement
27 that provides for postadoptive contact. If such information is withheld, an agent
28 who may receive service of process for the parent must be provided in the
29 agreement.
30 4. A parent or adoptive parent who enters into an agreement that provides
31 for postadoptive contact shall include in the agreement an address at which the
32 parent or adoptive parent may receive service of a petition filed pursuant to
33 section 150 of this act unless the parent or adoptive parent elects to receive
34 service by alternate means through electronic mail rather than certified or
35 registered mail, in which case, the electronic mail address must be included in the
36 agreement. If a parent or adoptive parent refuses or fails to include such an
37 address in an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact, the court may, on
38 the date on which the court enters an order of adoption which incorporates the
39 agreement, order the child-placing agency to provide the court with the contact
40 information of the parent or adoptive parent who refused or failed to include the
41 address. If a court so orders, the court shall:
42 (a) Append the address to the agreement for postadoptive contact; and
43 (b) Make the address available to any party to the agreement who wishes to
44 file a petition pursuant to section 150 of this act.
45 5. If a parent or adoptive parent changes the address that was included in
46 an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact pursuant to subsection 4, the
47 parent shall file with the clerk of the court notice of the change of address within
48 15 days after the change of address.
49 6. A court that enters an order of adoption which incorporates an
50 agreement that provides for postadoptive contact shall retain jurisdiction to
51 enforce, modify or terminate the agreement that provides for postadoptive contact
52 until:
53 (a) The child reaches 18 years of age;

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 47
1 (b) The child becomes emancipated; or
2 (c) The agreement is terminated.
3 7. The establishment of an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact
4 does not affect the rights of an adoptive parent as the legal parent of the child as
5 set forth in section 38 of this act.
6 Sec. 148. 1. Each prospective adoptive parent of a child to be adopted
7 who enters into an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact pursuant to
8 section 147 of this act shall notify the court responsible for entering the order of
9 adoption of the child of the existence of the agreement as soon as practicable
10 after the agreement is established, but not later than the time at which the court
11 enters the order of adoption of the child.
12 2. Each:
13 (a) Director or other authorized representative of the child-placing agency
14 involved in the adoption proceedings concerning the child; and
15 (b) Attorney representing a prospective adoptive parent, the child and the
16 child-placing agency in the adoption proceedings concerning the child,
17  shall, as soon as practicable after obtaining actual knowledge that the
18 prospective adoptive parent or parents of the child and the parent or parents of
19 the child have entered into an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact
20 pursuant to section 147 of this act, notify the court responsible for entering the
21 order of adoption of the child of the existence of the agreement.
22 Sec. 149. 1. Before a court may enter an order of adoption of a child, the
23 court must address:
24 (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection 2, each prospective adoptive
25 parent of the child to be adopted;
26 (b) Each director or other authorized representative of the child-placing
27 agency involved in the adoption proceedings concerning the child; and
28 (c) Each attorney representing a prospective adoptive parent, the child and
29 the child-placing agency in the adoption proceedings concerning the child,
30  and inquire whether the person has actual knowledge that the prospective
31 adoptive parent or parents of the child and parent or parents of the child have
32 entered into an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact pursuant to
33 section 147 of this act.
34 2. The court may for purposes of subsection 1 address a prospective
35 adoptive parent described in section 138 of this act by telephone or [video
36 conference.] remote appearance.
37 3. If the court determines that the prospective adoptive parent or parents
38 and the parent or parents have entered into an agreement that provides for
39 postadoptive contact, the court shall:
40 (a) Order the prospective adoptive parent or parents to provide a copy of the
41 agreement to the court; and
42 (b) Incorporate the agreement into the order of adoption.
43 Sec. 150. 1. A parent who has entered into an agreement that provides for
44 postadoptive contact pursuant to section 147 of this act may, for good cause
45 shown:
46 (a) Petition the court that entered the order of adoption of the child to prove
47 the existence of the agreement that provides for postadoptive contact and to
48 request that the agreement be incorporated into the order of adoption; and
49 (b) During the period set forth in subsection 2 of section 151 of this act,
50 petition the court that entered the order of adoption of the child to enforce the
51 terms of the agreement that provides for postadoptive contact if the agreement
52 complies with the requirements of subsection 2 of section 147 of this act.

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 48
1 2. An adoptive parent who has entered into an agreement that provides for
2 postadoptive contact pursuant to section 147 of this act may:
3 (a) During the period set forth in subsection 2 of section 151 of this act,
4 petition the court that entered the order of adoption of the child to enforce the
5 terms of the agreement that provides for postadoptive contact if the agreement
6 complies with the requirements of subsection 2 of section 147 of this act; and
7 (b) Petition the court that entered the order of adoption of the child to modify
8 or terminate the agreement that provides for postadoptive contact in the manner
9 set forth in section 152 of this act.
10 3. A petition filed pursuant to this section must be:
11 (a) Filed under the same case number as the proceeding for adoption;
12 (b) Served by the parent or adoptive parent who filed the petition using
13 certified or registered mail with return receipt requested, or if elected by any of
14 the parties to the postadoptive contact agreement to receive service by alternate
15 means through electronic mail, upon each other parent or adoptive parent, as
16 applicable, who has entered into the agreement that provides for postadoptive
17 contact at the address provided pursuant to subsection 4 or 5 of section 147 of
18 this act; and
19 (c) Heard by:
20 (1) If available, the judge who issued the order of adoption of the child;
21 (2) If the judge described in subparagraph (1) is unavailable and if a
22 family court has been established in the judicial district, a judge of the family
23 court; or
24 (3) If the judge described in subparagraph (1) is unavailable and if a
25 family court has not been established in the judicial district, any district judge of
26 the judicial district.
27 Sec. 151. 1. Failure to comply with the terms of an agreement that
28 provides for postadoptive contact entered into pursuant to section 147 of this act
29 may not be used as a ground to:
30 (a) Set aside an order of adoption;
31 (b) Revoke, nullify or set aside a valid specific consent to adoption or
32 relinquishment; or
33 (c) Except as otherwise provided in NRS 41.509, award any civil damages to
34 a party to the agreement.
35 2. Any action to enforce the terms of an agreement that provides for
36 postadoptive contact must be commenced not later than 120 days after the date on
37 which the agreement was breached.
38 Sec. 152. 1. An agreement that provides for postadoptive contact entered
39 into pursuant to section 147 of this act may only be modified or terminated by an
40 adoptive parent petitioning the court that entered the order which included the
41 agreement. The court may grant a request to modify or terminate the agreement
42 only if:
43 (a) The adoptive parent petitioning the court for the modification or
44 termination establishes that:
45 (1) A change in circumstances warrants the modification or termination;
46 and
47 (2) The contact provided for in the agreement is no longer in the best
48 interest of the child; or
49 (b) Each party to the agreement consents to the modification or termination.
50 2. If an adoptive parent petitions the court for a modification or termination
51 of an agreement pursuant to this section:
52 (a) There is a presumption that the modification or termination is in the best
53 interest of the child; and

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 49
1 (b) The court may consider the wishes of the child involved in the agreement.
2 3. Any order issued pursuant to this section to modify an agreement that
3 provides for postadoptive contact:
4 (a) May limit, restrict, condition or decrease contact between the parties
5 involved in the agreement; and
6 (b) May not expand or increase the contact between the parties involved in
7 the agreement or place any new obligation on an adoptive parent.
8 Sec. 153. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 3, it is unlawful
9 for any person to pay or offer to pay money or anything of value to the parent of
10 a child in return for the parent’s placement of the child for adoption, for the
11 execution of a specific consent to adoption or relinquishment or for the
12 cooperation in the adoption of the child.
13 2. It is unlawful for any person to receive payment for medical and other
14 necessary expenses related to the birth of a child from a prospective adoptive
15 parent with the intent of not consenting to or completing the adoption of the
16 child.
17 3. A person may pay the medical and other necessary living expenses
18 related to the birth of a child of another as an act of charity so long as the
19 payment is not contingent upon the parent’s placement of the child for adoption,
20 the execution of a specific consent to adoption or relinquishment or cooperation
21 in the adoption of the child.
22 4. This section does not prohibit a parent from refusing to place a child for
23 adoption after its birth.
24 5. The provisions of this section do not apply if a woman enters into a
25 lawful contract to act as a gestational carrier, as defined in NRS 126.580.
26 6. A person who violates:
27 (a) The provisions of subsection 1 is guilty of a category D felony and shall
28 be punished as provided in NRS 193.130.
29 (b) The provisions of subsection 2 is guilty of a gross misdemeanor.
30 7. As used in this section, “person” includes a hospital.
31 Sec. 154. NRS 125E.210 is hereby amended to read as follows:
32 125E.210 1. Except if the person already knows that a child is an Indian
33 child, whenever a person is required in a child custody proceeding to determine
34 whether there is reason to know that the child is an Indian child, the person shall
35 make a good faith effort to determine whether the child is an Indian child,
36 including, without limitation, by consulting with:
37 (a) The child;
38 (b) The child’s parent or parents;
39 (c) Any person having custody of the child or with whom the child resides;
40 (d) Extended family members of the child;
41 (e) Any other person who may reasonably be expected to have information
42 regarding the child’s membership or eligibility for membership in an Indian tribe;
43 and
44 (f) Any Indian tribe of which the child may be a member or of which the child
45 may be eligible for membership.
46 2. A court or person has reason to know that a child in a child custody
47 proceeding is an Indian child if:
48 (a) The person knows that the child is an Indian child;
49 (b) The court has found that the child is an Indian child or that there is reason
50 to know that the child is an Indian child;
51 (c) Any person present in the proceeding, officer of the court involved in the
52 proceeding, Indian tribe, Indian organization or agency informs the court or the

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 50
1 person that the child is an Indian child or that information has been discovered
2 indicating that the child is an Indian child;
3 (d) The child indicates to the court or the person that the child is an Indian
4 child;
5 (e) The court or the person is informed that the domicile or residence of the
6 child, the child’s parent or the child’s Indian custodian is on a reservation or in an
7 Alaska Native village;
8 (f) The court or the person is informed that the child is or has been a ward of a
9 tribal court;
10 (g) The court or the person is informed that the child or the child’s parent
11 possesses an identification card or other record indicating membership in an Indian
12 tribe;
13 (h) Testimony or documents presented to the court indicate in any way that the
14 child may be an Indian child; or
15 (i) Any other indicia provided to the court or the person, or within the
16 knowledge of the court or the person, indicates that the child is an Indian child.
17 3. Except as otherwise provided in [NRS 127.1867,] section 89 of this act,
18 whenever a person is required to demonstrate to the court in a child custody
19 proceeding that the person made efforts to determine whether a child is an Indian
20 child, the court shall make written findings regarding whether the person satisfied
21 the inquiry requirements under subsection 1 and whether the child is an Indian child
22 or whether there is reason to know that the child is an Indian child. At the
23 commencement of any hearing in an emergency proceeding or a child custody
24 proceeding, unless the court previously found that the child is an Indian child, the
25 court shall ask, on the record, each person present on the matter whether the person
26 has reason to know that the child is an Indian child and shall make a finding
27 regarding whether there is reason to know that the child is an Indian child.
28 4. If the court finds under subsection 3 that there is:
29 (a) Reason to know that the child is an Indian child but the court does not have
30 sufficient evidence to find that the child is an Indian child, the court shall order that
31 the inquiry as to whether the child is an Indian child continue until the court finds
32 that the child is not an Indian child.
33 (b) Not reason to know that the child is an Indian child, the court shall order
34 each party to immediately inform the court if the party receives information
35 providing reason to know that the child is an Indian child.
36 5. If the court finds under subsection 3 that there is reason to know that the
37 child is an Indian child but the court does not have sufficient evidence to make a
38 finding that the child is or is not an Indian child, the court shall require the
39 appropriate agency or other party to submit a report, declaration or testimony on the
40 record that the agency or other party used due diligence to identify and work with
41 all of the tribes of which the child may be a member or in which the child may be
42 eligible for membership to verify whether the child is a member or is eligible for
43 membership.
44 6. A person making an inquiry under this section shall request that any tribe
45 receiving information under this section keep documents and information regarding
46 the inquiry confidential.

14 Sec. 155. Chapter 127 of NRS is hereby amended by adding thereto the
15 provisions set forth as sections 156 to 168, inclusive, of this act.
16 Sec. 156. As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise requires, the
17 words and terms defined in sections 157 to 163, inclusive, of this act have the
18 meanings ascribed to them in those sections.
19 Sec. 157. “Home study” means the investigation of a prospective adoptive
20 parent or parents before an adoptive placement to determine the suitability of the
21 prospective adoptive home pursuant to NRS 127.2805.
22 Sec. 158. “Parent” means a person:
23 1. Who has legal rights, privileges, responsibilities and obligations to a
24 child and is a biological or legal parent of a child whose parental rights have not
25 been terminated by a court order or execution of a specific consent to adoption or
26 relinquishment;
27 2. Who is a putative parent or proven parent of a child;
28 3. Who is presumed to be the parent of a child;
29 4. Whose paternity or parentage has been established pursuant to chapter
30 126 of NRS; or
31 5. Whose parentage has been confirmed by a court order.
32 Sec. 159. “Placing parent” means a parent who executed a specific consent
33 to adoption or relinquishment pursuant to this chapter.
34 Sec. 160. “Post-placement investigation” means an investigation of the
35 prospective adoptive home after an adoptive placement pursuant to NRS 127.120.
36 Sec. 161. “Prospective adoptive parent” means a person with whom a child
37 has been placed for adoption but whose petition for adoption has not been
38 granted by the court.
39 Sec. 162. “Relinquishment” means a document that is executed in an
40 agency adoption which:
41 1. Terminates the parental rights of the person executing the document in
42 the child to be adopted; and
43 2. Places the child for adoption with a named child-placing agency.
44 Sec. 163. “Specific consent to adoption” means a document that is
45 executed in an identified adoption which:
46 1. Terminates or retains the parental right of the person executing the
47 document; and
48 2. Authorizes the child to be adopted by a specifically named person or
49 persons.
50 Sec. 163.5. An adoptive placement occurs when:
51 1. A parent executes a specific consent to adoption or relinquishment; or
52 2. A child-placing agency grants physical custody of a child in its custody to
53 a prospective adoptive parent or parents for adoption.

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 52
1 Sec. 164. Compliance with the requirements of the Interstate Compact on
2 the Placement of Children pursuant to NRS 127.320 to 127.350, inclusive, may be
3 performed by an agency which provides child welfare services, a child-placing
4 agency or an attorney licensed to practice law in this State.
5 Sec. 165. If a parent is considering consenting to an identified adoption,
6 the child-placing agency shall:
7 1. Provide information relating to the adoption process, information
8 concerning the State Register for Adoptions pursuant to section 33 of this act and
9 information relating to counseling services, which must be provided before the
10 parent signs the specific consent to adoption, for the purpose of ensuring that the
11 decision to consent to the adoption of the child is made without coercion and not
12 under duress or undue influence, and to make the placing parent aware of
13 counseling services which can be made available after the execution of the
14 specific consent to adoption to ensure that the placing parent is provided with
15 emotional support;
16 2. Provide information to the placing parent regarding alternatives to
17 adoption;
18 3. Obtain information regarding the background of the placing parent for
19 two or three generations, including, without limitation:
20 (a) The occurrence of any childhood diseases;
21 (b) Psychiatric and psychological histories;
22 (c) Demographic information and social history;
23 (d) Any use of drugs or alcohol;
24 (e) Abuse of alcohol;
25 (f) Blood types;
26 (g) Any congenital deformities;
27 (h) Prenatal history, including, without limitation, information concerning
28 the use of alcohol, drugs, tobacco and prescription medications during
29 pregnancy; and
30 (i) Any other pertinent information;
31 4. Obtain, if the child to be placed for adoption has already been born,
32 information regarding:
33 (a) The developmental and medical history of the child;
34 (b) The educational and social development of the child;
35 (c) The personal relationship between the child and the parent, including
36 their attitudes towards one another; and
37 (d) Any religious affiliation of the child;
38 5. Advise the placing parent that the placing parent may read the home
39 study of the prospective adoptive parent or parents identified in the specific
40 consent to adoption before the execution of the specific consent to adoption;
41 6. Facilitate a request pursuant to the Interstate Compact on the Placement
42 of Children, if required by NRS 127.330; and
43 7. Maintain a case file with a record of the information obtained and
44 services provided by the child-placing agency.

36 Sec. 167. 1. If a prospective adoptive parent or parents determine that an
37 identified adoption cannot or should not proceed, the adoptive parent or parents,
38 as applicable, may:
39 (a) Withdraw a petition for termination of parental rights or a petition for
40 adoption; and
41 (b) Declare the specific consent to adoption void and surrender the adoptive
42 placement.
43 2. The declaration surrendering the adoptive placement pursuant to
44 subsection 1 must:
45 (a) Be in writing, notarized and acknowledged by the surrendering
46 prospective adoptive parent or parents; and
47 (b) Give notice to all parents of the child, the court of competent jurisdiction
48 and the child-placing agency, if applicable.

50 surrendering an adoptive placement pursuant to subsection 1, the prospective
51 adoptive parent or parents must:

1 (b) If the placing parent or parents decline to accept the child, the placing

4 4. A specific consent to adoption declared void is without legal effect and
5 the parental rights are restored.
6 5. An adoptive placement may not be surrendered after an order finalizing
7 the adoption has been entered by the court.
8 Sec. 168. 1. If a court of competent jurisdiction determines that a parent
9 has legal rights to a child making the child ineligible for an agency adoption, the
10 child-placing agency shall:
11 (a) Immediately declare the relinquishment executed by the placing parent
12 null and void and without legal effect;
13 (b) Immediately withdraw the petition for termination of parental rights; and
14 (c) Provide the court with a declaration that is notarized and acknowledged
15 by the child-placing agency that the relinquishment has been voided.
16 2. If a relinquishment is voided pursuant to subsection 1, all legal rights,
17 privileges, responsibilities and obligations to a child are restored to the placing
18 parent by operation of law.

30 (2) The court has determined, after a hearing, that the agreement is in the
31 best interest of the child.] The agreement is signed by the parent or parents
32 before:
33 (1) The termination or voluntary relinquishment of the parental rights of
34 the parent or parents; or
35 (2) The execution of a specific consent to adoption or relinquishment.
36 3. The identity of a [natural] parent is not required to be included in an
37 agreement that provides for postadoptive contact. If such information is withheld,
38 an agent who may receive service of process for the [natural] parent must be
39 provided in the agreement.
40 4. A [natural] parent or adoptive parent who enters into an agreement that
41 provides for postadoptive contact shall include in the agreement an address at
42 which the [natural] parent or adoptive parent may receive service of a petition filed
43 pursuant to NRS 127.1885 [.] , unless the parent or adoptive parent elects to
44 receive service by alternate means through electronic mail rather than certified
45 or registered mail, in which case, the electronic mail address must be included in
46 the agreement. If a [natural] parent or adoptive parent refuses or fails to include
47 such an address in an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact, the court
48 may, on the date on which the court enters an order [or decree] of adoption which
49 incorporates the agreement, order the child-placing agency [which provides child
50 welfare services] to provide the court with the contact information of the [natural]
51 parent or adoptive parent who refused or failed to include [his or her] the address. If
52 a court so orders, the court shall:
53 (a) Append the address to the agreement for postadoptive contact; and

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 68
1 (b) Make the address available to any party to the agreement who wishes to file
2 a petition pursuant to NRS 127.1885.
3 5. If a [natural] parent or adoptive parent changes [his or her] the address that
4 was included in an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact pursuant to
5 subsection 4, the parent shall file with the clerk of the court notice of the change of
6 address within 15 days after the change of address.
7 6. A court that enters an order [or decree] of adoption which incorporates an
8 agreement that provides for postadoptive contact shall retain jurisdiction to enforce,
9 modify or terminate the agreement that provides for postadoptive contact until:
10 (a) The child reaches 18 years of age;
11 (b) The child becomes emancipated; or
12 (c) The agreement is terminated.
13 7. The establishment of an agreement that provides for postadoptive contact
14 does not affect the rights of an adoptive parent as the legal parent of the child as set
15 forth in [NRS 127.160.] section 38 of this act.

22 of the custody and control of, and terminating the parental rights of the parent or
23 parents with respect to the child, and declaring the child to be free from such
24 custody or control, and placing the custody and control of the child in some person
25 or agency qualified by the laws of this State to provide services and care to
26 children, or to receive any children for placement. The termination of parental
27 rights pursuant to this section does not terminate the right of the child to inherit
28 from his or her parent or parents, except that the right to inherit terminates if the
29 child is adopted as provided in [NRS 127.160.] section 38 of this act.
30 2. If the child is placed in the custody and control of a person or agency
31 qualified by the laws of this State to receive children for placement, the person or
32 agency, in seeking to place the child:
33 (a) May give preference to the placement of the child with any person related
34 within the fifth degree of consanguinity to the child whom the person or agency
35 finds suitable and able to provide proper care and guidance for the child, regardless
36 of whether the relative resides within this State.
37 (b) Shall, if practicable, give preference to the placement of the child together
38 with his or her siblings.
39  Any search for a relative with whom to place a child pursuant to this subsection
40 must be completed within 1 year after the initial placement of the child outside of
41 his or her home.

1 2. A governmental entity may not reject a book or record which is
2 copyrighted solely because it is copyrighted.
3 3. A governmental entity that has legal custody or control of a public book or
4 record shall not deny a request made pursuant to subsection 1 to inspect or copy or
5 receive a copy of a public book or record on the basis that the requested public
6 book or record contains information that is confidential if the governmental entity
7 can redact, delete, conceal or separate, including, without limitation, electronically,
8 the confidential information from the information included in the public book or
9 record that is not otherwise confidential.
10 4. If requested, a governmental entity shall provide a copy of a public record
11 in an electronic format by means of an electronic medium. Nothing in this
12 subsection requires a governmental entity to provide a copy of a public record in an
13 electronic format or by means of an electronic medium if:
14 (a) The public record:
15 (1) Was not created or prepared in an electronic format; and
16 (2) Is not available in an electronic format; or
17 (b) Providing the public record in an electronic format or by means of an
18 electronic medium would:
19 (1) Give access to proprietary software; or
20 (2) Require the production of information that is confidential and that
21 cannot be redacted, deleted, concealed or separated from information that is not
22 otherwise confidential.

16 432B.190 The Division of Child and Family Services shall, in consultation

18 1. Regulations establishing reasonable and uniform standards for:
19 (a) Child welfare services provided in this State;
20 (b) Programs for the prevention of abuse or neglect of a child and the
21 achievement of the permanent placement of a child;
22 (c) The development of local councils involving public and private
23 organizations;
24 (d) Reports of abuse or neglect, records of these reports and the response to
25 these reports;
26 (e) Carrying out the provisions of NRS 432B.260, including, without
27 limitation, the qualifications of persons with whom agencies which provide child
28 welfare services enter into agreements to provide services to children and families;
29 (f) The management and assessment of reported cases of abuse or neglect;
30 (g) The protection of the legal rights of parents and children;
31 (h) Emergency shelter for a child;
32 (i) The prevention, identification and correction of abuse or neglect of a child
33 in residential institutions;
34 (j) Developing and distributing to persons who are responsible for a child’s
35 welfare a pamphlet that is written in language which is easy to understand, is
36 available in English and in any other language the Division determines is
37 appropriate based on the demographic characteristics of this State and sets forth:
38 (1) Contact information regarding persons and governmental entities which
39 provide assistance to persons who are responsible for the welfare of children,
40 including, without limitation, persons and entities which provide assistance to
41 persons who are being investigated for allegedly abusing or neglecting a child;
42 (2) The procedures for taking a child for placement in protective custody;
43 and
44 (3) The state and federal legal rights of:
45 (I) A person who is responsible for a child’s welfare and who is the
46 subject of an investigation of alleged abuse or neglect of a child, including, without
47 limitation, the legal rights of such a person at the time an agency which provides
48 child welfare services makes initial contact with the person in the course of the
49 investigation and at the time the agency takes the child for placement in protective
50 custody, and the legal right of such a person to be informed of any allegation of
51 abuse or neglect of a child which is made against the person at the initial time of
52 contact with the person by the agency; and

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 84
1 (II) Persons who are parties to a proceeding held pursuant to NRS
2 432B.410 to 432B.590, inclusive, during all stages of the proceeding; and
3 (k) Making the necessary inquiries required pursuant to NRS 432B.397 to
4 determine whether a child is an Indian child.
5 2. Regulations, which are applicable to any person who is authorized to place
6 a child in protective custody without the consent of the person responsible for the
7 child’s welfare, setting forth reasonable and uniform standards for establishing
8 whether immediate action is necessary to protect the child from injury, abuse or
9 neglect for the purposes of determining whether to place the child into protective
10 custody pursuant to NRS 432B.390. Such standards must consider the potential
11 harm to the child in remaining in his or her home, including, without limitation:
12 (a) Circumstances in which a threat of harm suggests that a child is in
13 imminent danger of serious harm.
14 (b) The conditions or behaviors of the child’s family which threaten the safety
15 of the child who is unable to protect himself or herself and who is dependent on
16 others for protection, including, without limitation, conditions or behaviors that are
17 beyond the control of the caregiver of the child and create an imminent threat of
18 serious harm to the child.
19  The Division of Child and Family Services shall ensure that the appropriate
20 persons or entities to whom the regulations adopted pursuant to this subsection
21 apply are provided with a copy of such regulations. As used in this subsection,
22 “serious harm” includes the threat or evidence of serious physical injury, sexual
23 abuse, significant pain or mental suffering, extreme fear or terror, extreme
24 impairment or disability, death, substantial impairment or risk of substantial
25 impairment to the child’s mental or physical health or development.
26 3. Regulations establishing procedures for:
27 (a) Expeditiously locating any missing child who has been placed in the
28 custody of an agency which provides child welfare services;
29 (b) Determining the primary factors that contributed to a child who has been
30 placed in the custody of an agency which provides child welfare services running
31 away or otherwise being absent from foster care, and to the extent possible and
32 appropriate, responding to those factors in current and subsequent placements; and
33 (c) Determining the experiences of a child who has been placed in the custody
34 of an agency which provides child welfare services during any period the child was
35 missing, including, without limitation, determining whether the child may be a
36 victim of sexual abuse or sexual exploitation.
37 4. Such other regulations as are necessary for:
38 (a) The administration of NRS 432B.010 to 432B.606, inclusive.
39 (b) The implementation of [NRS 125E.010 to 125E.370, inclusive,] chapter
40 127E of NRS and NRS 127.041, [127.115,] 127.151 , [and] 127.1861 [to 127.1869,
41 inclusive.] , 127.1863 and 127.1865, and sections 64, 74, 80, 86 to 90, inclusive,
42 127, 140, 144, 145 and 146 of this act.
43 Sec. 230. NRS 432B.393 is hereby amended to read as follows:
44 432B.393 1. Except as otherwise provided in this section, an agency which
45 provides child welfare services shall make reasonable efforts to preserve and
46 reunify the family of a child:
47 (a) Before the placement of the child in foster care, to prevent or eliminate the
48 need to remove the child from the home; and
49 (b) To make it possible for the safe return of the child to the home.
50 2. In determining the reasonable efforts required by subsection 1, the health
51 and safety of the child must be the paramount concern. The agency which provides
52 child welfare services may make reasonable efforts to place the child for adoption
53 or with a legal guardian concurrently with making the reasonable efforts required

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 85
1 pursuant to subsection 1. If the court determines that continuation of the reasonable
2 efforts required by subsection 1 is inconsistent with the plan for the permanent
3 placement of the child, the agency which provides child welfare services shall make
4 reasonable efforts to place the child in a timely manner in accordance with that plan
5 and to complete whatever actions are necessary to finalize the permanent placement
6 of the child.
7 3. An agency which provides child welfare services is not required to make
8 the reasonable efforts required by subsection 1 if the court finds that:
9 (a) A parent or other person responsible for the child’s welfare has:
10 (1) Committed, aided or abetted in the commission of, or attempted,
11 conspired or solicited to commit murder or voluntary manslaughter;
12 (2) Caused the abuse or neglect of the child, or of another child of the
13 parent or other person responsible for the child’s welfare, which resulted in
14 substantial bodily harm to the abused or neglected child;
15 (3) Caused the abuse or neglect of the child, a sibling of the child or
16 another child in the household, and the abuse or neglect was so extreme or
17 repetitious as to indicate that any plan to return the child to the home would result
18 in an unacceptable risk to the health or welfare of the child; or
19 (4) Abandoned the child for 60 or more days, and the identity of the parent
20 of the child is unknown and cannot be ascertained through reasonable efforts;
21 (b) A parent of the child has, for the previous 6 months, had the ability to
22 contact or communicate with the child and made no more than token efforts to do
23 so;
24 (c) The parental rights of a parent to a sibling of the child have been terminated
25 by a court order upon any basis other than the execution of a voluntary
26 relinquishment of those rights by a natural parent, and the court order is not
27 currently being appealed;
28 (d) The child or a sibling of the child was previously removed from the home,
29 adjudicated to have been abused or neglected, returned to the home and
30 subsequently removed from the home as a result of additional abuse or neglect;
31 (e) The child is less than 1 year of age, the father of the child is not married to
32 the mother of the child and the father of the child:
33 (1) Has failed within 60 days after learning of the birth of the child, to visit
34 the child, to commence proceedings to establish his paternity of the child or to
35 provide financial support for the child; or
36 (2) Is entitled to seek custody of the child but fails to do so within 60 days
37 after learning that the child was placed in foster care;
38 (f) The child was delivered to a provider of emergency services pursuant to
39 NRS 432B.630;
40 (g) The child, a sibling of the child or another child in the household has been
41 sexually abused or has been subjected to neglect by pervasive instances of failure to
42 protect the child from sexual abuse; or
43 (h) A parent of the child is required to register as a sex offender pursuant to the
44 provisions of chapter 179D of NRS or the provisions of the federal Adam Walsh
45 Child Protection and Safety Act of 2006, 34 U.S.C. §§ 20901 et seq.
46 4. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 6, for the purposes of this
47 section, unless the context otherwise requires, “reasonable efforts” have been made
48 if an agency which provides child welfare services to children with legal custody of
49 a child has exercised diligence and care in arranging appropriate, accessible and
50 available services that are designed to improve the ability of a family to provide a
51 safe and stable home for each child in the family, with the health and safety of the
52 child as its paramount concerns. The exercise of such diligence and care includes,
53 without limitation, obtaining necessary and appropriate information concerning the

Senate Amendment No. 671 to Assembly Bill No. 227 First Reprint Page 86
1 child for the purposes of NRS 127.152, 127.410 and 424.038 , and section 81 of
2 this act, and, if necessary, creating an in-home safety plan for the protection of the
3 child.
4 5. In determining whether reasonable efforts have been made pursuant to
5 subsection 4, the court shall:
6 (a) Evaluate the evidence and make findings based on whether a reasonable
7 person would conclude that reasonable efforts were made;
8 (b) Consider any input from the child;
9 (c) Consider the efforts made and the evidence presented since the previous
10 finding of the court concerning reasonable efforts;
11 (d) Consider the diligence and care that the agency is legally authorized and
12 able to exercise, including, without limitation, the efforts to create an in-home
13 safety plan;
14 (e) Recognize and take into consideration the legal obligations of the agency to
15 comply with any applicable laws and regulations;
16 (f) Base its determination on the circumstances and facts concerning the
17 particular family or plan for the permanent placement of the child at issue;
18 (g) Consider whether any of the efforts made were contrary to the health and
19 safety of the child;
20 (h) Consider the efforts made, if any, to prevent the need to remove the child
21 from the home and to finalize the plan for the permanent placement of the child;
22 (i) Consider whether the provisions of subsection 6 are applicable; and
23 (j) Consider any other matters the court deems relevant.
24 6. An agency which provides child welfare services may satisfy the
25 requirement of making reasonable efforts pursuant to this section by taking no
26 action concerning a child or making no effort to provide services to a child if it is
27 reasonable, under the circumstances, to do so.
28 7. In determining whether reasonable efforts are not required pursuant to
29 subsection 3 or whether reasonable efforts have been made pursuant to subsection
30 4, the court shall ensure that each determination is:
31 (a) Made by the court on a case-by-case basis;
32 (b) Based upon specific evidence; and
33 (c) Expressly stated by the court in its order.
34 8. As used in this section, “in-home safety plan” means a plan created by an
35 agency which provides child welfare services to ensure the protection of a child in
36 [his or her] the home, including, without limitation, determining any vulnerabilities
37 of the child, managing any potential threats to the safety of the child and
38 determining the capacity of the person responsible for the welfare of the child to
39 care for the child.

1 the placement must be reviewed by the court at least semiannually, and within 90

5 432B.585.
6 2. An agency acting as the custodian of the child shall, before any hearing for
7 review of the placement of a child, submit a report to the court, or to the panel if it
8 has been designated to review the matter, which includes:
9 (a) An evaluation of the progress of the child and the family of the child and
10 any recommendations for further supervision, treatment or rehabilitation.
11 (b) Information concerning the placement of the child in relation to the child’s
12 siblings, including, without limitation:
13 (1) Whether the child was placed together with the siblings;
14 (2) Any efforts made by the agency to have the child placed together with
15 the siblings;
16 (3) Any actions taken by the agency to ensure that the child has contact
17 with the siblings; and
18 (4) If the child is not placed together with the siblings:
19 (I) The reasons why the child is not placed together with the siblings;
20 and
21 (II) A plan for the child to visit the siblings, which must be presented
22 at the first hearing to occur after the siblings are separated and approved by the
23 court. The plan for visitation must be updated as necessary to reflect any change in
24 the placement of the child or a sibling, including, without limitation, any such
25 change that occurs after the termination of parental rights to the child or a sibling or
26 the adoption of a sibling.
27 (c) Information concerning the child’s education, including:

41 (7) A summary of any special education services received by the child;

44 most recent semester, if applicable;
45 (10) A statement of the number of times the child has been absent from
46 school during the current or most recent school year for which the child was
47 enrolled in school;
48 (11) The scores the child received on any academic assessments or
49 standardized examinations administered to the child;
50 (12) Any information provided by the educational decision maker
51 appointed for the child pursuant to NRS 432B.462; and
